#  Siege Weapons
These weapons have been engineered for large-scale warfare against enemy armies and settlements. What sets them apart from other weapons is their size and the number of creatures required to operate them effectively (generally more than two). These weapons range from highly sophisticated cannons and rocket launchers to crude catapults and giant slingshots. Regardless of their form, they are all large enough that moving them is a slow process and labor-intensive enough to use that they require a team of creatures to operate them effectively.

## Repairing Weapons
If a weapon has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting to repair the damage. The creature must have the necessary tools and parts for the repairs. After 1 hour of repair work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus to the check if it is proficient with the required tools. If the check succeeds, the weapon regains 2d4 + the creature's Intelligence modifier + the creature's proficiency bonus hit points. If the check fails, the weapon does not regain any hit points, but the repair can be attempted again using the same tools and replacement parts.

\columnbreak

## Siege Weapon Attributes
In addition to the common attributes of size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity, these weapons have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Hit Points 
A weapon has hit points that can be restored through repairs. When its hit points reach 0, the weapon becomes inoperative and irreparably damaged. 

Many weapons have a damage threshold. Any source of damage less than this threshold only inflicts superficial damage and doesn't lower the weapon's hit points.

### Weapon DC 
The weapon's DC is used whenever a creature makes a check to fix mishaps, when a creature is repairing the weapon, or the weapon forces a creature to make a saving throw.

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies equipped with fully functioning siege weapons, the encounter's challenge rating (CR) should be calculated as if the weapon is an additional creature with its own CR.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/JjYPNWK/Unleash-Shell-The-Brothers-War-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-40px; right:0px; width:820px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:200px; right:100px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(15deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:249px; right:-200px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />



\pagebreakNum



### Ammo / Fuel
Weapons may require ammunition, such as bullets, or fuel, such as flammable chemicals, to make attacks. This part of the stat block includes the cost of the ammo and the number of charges it has, which represents the number of times the weapon can be used before it needs to be reloaded.

### Functions
By default, siege weapons have three different functions, which can each be activated as an action by its operators: Prep, Load, and Fire. Each function can only be performed once per round unless it states otherwise. Creatures within reach of a creature performing one of these functions can make opportunity attacks against them.

#### Prep
Siege weapons need to be prepped in different ways between being fired. This preparation could be cranking a ballista or cleaning the barrel of a cannon. Many siege weapons have multiple Prep functions that must be performed before they can be used again. In these cases, the different Prep actions can be done by different creatures within the same round. Unless stated otherwise, all the Prep functions must be completed before the weapon can be loaded.

### Siege Weapons: Art Credit
* Unleash Shell - Campbell White, Wizards of the Coast
* Goblin Artillery - Alex Horley-Orlandelli, Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

#### Load
This function is used to reload the weapon's ammunition up to its full capacity. It requires the creature loading it to have immediate access to the weapon's ammunition. If a creature doing the loading is hit by an opportunity it provoked by doing this, it drops the ammo and wastes its action.

#### Fire
This function is used to aim and fire the weapon at a target chosen by the creature performing the function.

### Passive Traits
This section describes any traits of the weapon has that don't require actions to utilize.

### Mishaps table
Some weapons can suffer a malfunction when certain functions are used. When such an event occurs, it will suffer a mishap and need to roll on its Mishap Table to determine what adverse effect it suffers. 

A creature can attempt to resolve a mishap by using its action to make an ability check based on the nature of the mishap. The creature making the check can be any member of the weapons team or anyone else within reach of the weapon. If the creature is proficient with the tools required for repairs and has them at hand, it adds its proficiency bonus to the check. A successful check ends the mishap. Mishaps that do not have a Repair Check Type cannot be repaired.

<img src='https://64.media.tumblr.com/97957bfd89fc58990ebbe31b4b543960/a95157cb330b1736-23/s1280x1920/c9807add3c7fc2bd781c456d1f8a9cee5de0f6e2.png' style='position:absolute; botom:-0px; right:0px; width:820px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-485px; right:-100px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(8deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-455px; right:-200px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-2deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-451px; right:-00px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-4deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

\pagebreakNum

# Howdahs
War howdahs are small armored structured mounted to the backs of large war beasts that can hold multiple creatures. 

The following rules can help you codify how to use different types of howdahs in your games. They can be applied to howdahs of different shapes and sizes and used as tools for designing your own howdahs. 

## Howdah Rules
Howdahs are generally structures that provide cover to multiple creatures mounted on a larger war beast of some kind. The creatures within the howdah are referred to as riders, and the creature the howdah is mounted upon is referred to as its steed. If one of the riders is controlling the steed, that creature is the pilot. Howdah riders and steeds follow the mounted combat rules described in the Player's Handbook, but with the following differences:

### Movement & Initiative

* **Forced Movement.** If an effect moves a howdah or its steed, the howdah and its steed are moved together.

* **Controlled & Independant Steeds.** The howdah's steed can be a controlled or independent mount as described in the player's handbook. If it is controlled, there must be a pilot who is controlling it.



\columnbreak

* **Entering & Exiting Howdahs.** While there is space in the howdah, a creature can spend all its movement to enter or leave the howdah or only half its movement if it has a climbing speed. While the steed is not incapacitated, it can make an opposed Strength (Athletics) check against a creature attempting to enter the howdah. If the steed succeeds, the creature can't enter the howdah. Any movement it used to try to enter the howdah is wasted, and it can't try to enter again until the start of its next turn. Each passenger already inside the howdah may use its reaction to make an opportunity attack against the creature entering or exiting the howdah.



### Howdah Saving Throws
While objects normally automatically fail all Strength, Dexterity, and Constituion saving throws, howdahs are active parts of combat, meaning it often doesn't make sense for them to ignore effects that deal types of damage they are not immune to. As such, you can use the following rules when howdahs are subject to such saving throws.



<img src='https://i.ibb.co/GtD871x/Linebreaker-Baloth-Dominaria-United-Mt-G-Art-1024x752.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-110px; right:-80px; width:930px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img 
  src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;left:-290px;bottom:95px;transform:rotate(-8deg)' />

<img 
  src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;left:-290px;bottom:140px;transform:rotate(0deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

#### Strength & Dexterity Saves
Howdahs equipped on an unencumbered steed do not automatically fail their Strength and Dexterity saving throws, as they can rely on their steed to make the save for them. If a howdah is subjected to a Strength or Dexterity saving throw, its steed must make the saving throw against the effect. If the steed succeeds on the save, the howdah passes the save.

#### Constitution Saves
Howdahs can make their own Constitution saving throws against effects capable of damaging them and have their own modifier they apply to these saves. The howdah may make these saves regardless of whether or not it is mounted on a steed.

### Opportunity Attacks
When the howdah steed provokes an opportunity attack, the attacker can target the howdah itself. Passengers cannot provoke opportunity attacks from creatures outside the howdah.

### Spacing Within Howdah
All creatures inside a howdah are considered to be within 5 feet of each other.

### Prone Howdahs
If the steed is knocked prone, the howdah takes bludgeoning damage equal to a roll of three of the steed's largest hit dice.

### Teleporting
If the steed is teleported, the howdah and its riders can choose to teleport with it.

### Falling Howdahs
When a howdah's steed falls from a height of 10 feet or more, it and all its riders take fall damage as usual, and the riders fall prone.

### Repairing Howdahs
If a howdah has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting repairs, provided it has the necessary tools and parts. After 1 hour of work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus if proficient with the required tools. On success, the howdah regains 2d4 + the creature's Intelligence modifier + its proficiency bonus hit points. On failure, the howdah doesn't regain any hit points, but repairs can be reattempted with the same tools and parts.

### Howdah Destruction
When a howdah is destroyed, riders that were in it are knocked prone and land in unoccupied spaces within 5 feet of its steed.

<br>

\columnbreak


## Howdah Attributes
Besides the size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity attributes common to all objects, howdahs have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Howdah DC 
Whenever the howdah requires a creature to make a check or saving throw, that creature uses this value for the DC.

### Damage Threshold
Most howdahs possess bulk or armor that enables them to withstand minor hits. A howdah with a damage threshold is immune to all damage unless the amount of damage it takes is equal to or greater than its damage threshold value. In such cases, the howdah takes the damage as usual. Damage that fails to meet or exceed the howdah's damage threshold is considered superficial and does not reduce the howdah's hit points.

###  Steed Size
This is the minimum size a creature must be to be the howdah's steed. If a creature ever becomes too small to carry the howdah, the howdah falls off the creature and is knocked over as though its steed was knocked prone, described in the Prone Howdahs section.

### Creature Capacity 
Creature capacity determines the number of creatures that can ride in the howdah comfortably. Additional creatures may be able to fit by squeezing or clinging to the outside of the howdah at the DM's discretion.

### Constitution Modifier
This is the modifier the howdah adds to any Constitution saves it makes. 

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies that are equipped with a fully functioning howdah, the challenge rating (CR) of the encounter should be calculated as if the howdah is an additional creature with its own CR.

### Passive Traits
This section describes any traits the howdah has that don't
require actions to utilize.

### Siege Weapons
A howdah may have one or more built-in siege weapons. These siege weapons are built into the howdah and share its Hit Points, AC, and Damage Threshold and are destroyed when the howdah is destroyed. These siege weapons can only be operated by riders in the howdah, and riders can't provoke attacks of opportunity from creatures outside the howdah while operating these weapons. The weapons can't be used if the howdah is not attached to a steed or the steed is prone.

\pagebreakNum

## Lizardmen Howdahs

When lizardmen deploy their most titanic reptilian jungle monsters in combat, they are sometimes equipped with mighty war howdahs crewed by smaller lizardmen such as skinks. These howahs are wooden structures that allow an entire lizardman crew to ride atop a mighty steed. The structure provides cover for the crew and can be equppied with siege weapons and even an arcane Engine of the Gods which provides the lizardmen with magical aid. Most lizardmen monsters are far too wild to allow such structures on their back, so those that can be equipped this way are prized by the lizardmen.

___
> ## Large Howdah
>*Large howdah, 600 lbs.*
> ___
> - **Howdah DC** 15
> - **Armor Class** 15
> - **Hit Points** 75 (Damage threshold 10)
> - **Damage Immunities** Poison, Psychic 
> - **Steed Size** Huge
> - **Creature Capacity** 5 Medium creatures
> - **Constitution Modifier** +3
> - **Challenge** 1 (200 XP)     
> ___
>
> ***Howdah Protection.*** Creatures within the howdah have three-quarters cover from attacks and effects originating from outside the howdah as long as the howdah is attached to a steed that is not prone. To make a melee attack against a target in the howdah while outside of it, a creature must be within 5 feet of the steed, and if the attacking creature isn’t Large or larger, the attack must have a reach of at least 10 feet.

To make a melee attack against a target in the howdah while outside of it, a creature must be within 5 feet of the steed, and if the attacking creature isn’t Huge or larger, the attack must have a reach of at least 10 feet.

### Lizardmen Howdah Upgrades

Large howdahs and huge howdahs can be given any of the following upgrades. Each upgrade increases the howdahs effective CR by 1 unless its states otherwise.


#### Sacred Howdah
*The howdah is not only an instrument of war but a small shrine complete with relics and offerings dedicated to the Old Ones to curry their favor.*

The howdah counts as a magic object, and the three-quarters cover granted by the howdah gives a +5 bonus to all saving throws from effects outside the howdah, not just Dexterity saves. If a creature in the howdah is subjected to an effect from outside that allows it to make a saving throw to take only half damage, it takes no damage if it succeeds on the saving throw, and half damage if it fails.

#### Poison Ballista 

*The howdah is equipped with a ballista whose bolts are tipped with deadly jungle toxins.*

The howdah is equipped with the poison ballista siege weapon.
___
> ## Poison Ballista 
> *Medium siege weapon*
>___
> - **Weapon DC** 15
> - **Armor Class** 15 
> - **Hit Points** 60 (damage threshold: 5)
>___
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic
> - **Ammo** Poison Bolt (1 round, 100g)
> - **Challenge** 1 (200 XP)
> ___
>
> ### Functions
>
> ***Load.*** The weapon is loaded with a Poison Bolt. This must be done before it is prepped.
>
> ***Prep.*** The weapon is prepped to fire its next shot. This prep must be done while it is loaded.
>
> ***Fire.*** The ballista fires a bolt that flies in a straight line up to 480 feet in the direction of the user's choice before falling to the ground. If the bolt would strike a target, that target must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw. The target has advantage on the saving throw if the bolt has flown 120 feet or more. On a failed save, the target takes 33 (6d10) piercing damage and is inflicted with Jungle Toxins. If the target is reduced to 0 hit points or destroyed, the bolt keeps flying and deals 11 (2d10) less damage if it hits another target. Otherwise, the bolt's flight ends at the target's location. 

\columnbreak

#### Giant Blowpipe  
*The howdah is equipped with a giant blowpipe capable of firing a hail of poison-tipped darts.*

The howdah is equipped with the giant blowpipe siege weapon.
___
> ## Giant Blowpipe 
> *Medium siege weapon*
>___
> - **Weapon DC** 15
> - **Armor Class** 15 
> - **Hit Points** 60 (damage threshold: 5)
>___
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic
> - **Ammo** Poison Dart Cluster (1 round, 100g)
> - **Challenge** 1 (200 XP)
> ___
>
> ### Functions
>
> ***Load.*** The weapon is loaded with a Poison Dart Cluster. This must be done before it is prepped.
>
> ***Prep.*** The weapon is prepped to fire its next shot. This prep must be done while it is loaded.
>
> ***Fire.*** The blowpipe fires a barrage of darts that rain down at a point of the user's choice within 120 feet. Each creature in a 5-foot radius centered on that point must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 12 (5d4) piercing damage, is inflicted with Jungle Toxins, and makes the saving throw at the end of its turn against the toxins with disadvantage. On a successful save, a creature takes half damage, is still inflicted with Jungle Toxins, but does not have disadvantage on the saving throw at the end of its turn against the toxins.

<br>

> ##### Jungle Toxins
> At the end of the turn, each creature hit by one or more weapons that inflict Jungle Toxins must succeed on a DC 13 Constitution saving throw or be poisoned for 1 hour. A creature that has been hit by two or more attacks from weapons with Jungle Toxins this turn makes the saving throw with disadvantage. The target repeats the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success or taking 5 (2d4) poison damage on a failure.

\pagebreakNum

#### Engine of the Gods 
*The howdah is equipped with a sacred relic of the Old Ones capable of unleashing a variety of magical effects by those familiar with its usage.*

A howdah is equipped with an Engine of the Gods, which causes the howdah to be treated as a magical object. The engine has 3 charges by default and can possess up to 3 of the abilities listed below. Riders with the howdah who have proficiency in Religion and a Wisdom and Intelligence of 14 or higher can use their action to expend 1 charge to activate one of the engine's abilities. The engine regains all expended charges daily at dawn.

The Engine of the Gods increases the CR of the Howdah by 4 rather than 1.

##### Burning Alignment 
*As the engine comes into alignment, magical power is unleashed to scour the enemy.*

A vertical column of divine fire, 10 feet in radius and 100 feet high, descends at a point within 300 feet of the howdah of the user's choice. It then moves 30 feet horizontally in a straight line in the direction of the user's choice before dissipating. Each target the column passes through must make a DC 17 Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 14 (4d6) fire damage and 14 (4d6) radiant damage on a failed save and half as much damage on a successful save.  

##### Portent of Warding
*Mysterious power pours from the engine, protecting nearby allies.*

When activating this ability, the rider chooses any number of creatures, and an aura of eldritch warding radiates from the howdah in a 30-foot radius for one minute. Each chosen creature gains resistance to damage from spells while within the aura.

#### Howdahs: Art Credit
* Linebreaker Baloth - Brent Hollowell, Wizards of the Coast
* Naya - Zoltan Boros & Gabor Szikszai, Wizards of the Coast
* Mastermind's Acquisition - Svetlin Velinov, <br> Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

##### Arcane Configuration
*The engine siphons the winds of magic to aid in casting spells of specific energy.*

When activating this ability, the rider chooses a damage type and any number of creatures within 30 feet. The rider and all the chosen creatures then become empowered until the start of the rider's next turn. The next time an empowered creature casts a spell dealing the chosen damage type, it rolls three additional damage dice. The rider activating this ability can also cast a spell with a casting time of 1 action as a bonus action on the same turn.

##### Time Slows
*The engine bends the flow of time.*

Each creature in a 15-foot-radius sphere centered on a point within 300 feet of the howdah must make a DC 17 Charisma saving throw or be affected by the *slow* spell until the howdah is destroyed. A creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success. If it fails the repeat saving throw by 5 or more (DC 12), it is stunned until the effect ends.



##### Healing Light
*The engine releases a burst of light that heals battle-weary allies.*

When activating this ability, the rider chooses any number of creatures within 30 feet. Each chosen creature regains 18 (4d8) hit points.

##### Sacred Summon
*The engine calls to the heavens to summon a champion.*

A sacred saurian appears in an unoccupied space within 60 feet of the howdah of the rider's choice and remains until it or the howdah is reduced to 0 hit points or 10 minutes have passed. The saurian shares the initiative count of the rider who used the ability, and it takes its turn immediately after. The saurian is an ally to the rider and its companions.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/Pt2Zj21/masterminds-aquisition.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-300px; right:-80px; width:900px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img 
  src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;left:-170px;bottom:-80px;transform:rotate(0deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

# Lizardmen Forces

This section lists the different types of lizardmen along with the primeval creatures they often utilize in battle. The different species of lizardmen include the crox, the saurian, and the skinks. The various reptilian monsters they utilize can be found living alongside the lizardmen or wandering the wilds of their jungle homeland. 

### Blessings of the Old Ones

Some lizardmen are born with enhanced abilities attributed to their ancient gods. The same can even be true for the reptilian creatures they use in battle. These creatures bear colorations that signify their specialized abilities and the unique ways they can serve their masters. You can apply one of these blessings to any of the creature stat blocks described in this document, so long as it has a bite attack and the Primal Instinct trait. Doing so increases its CR by 1. 

Note that some blessings may not make sense for some creatures, such as applying the Blessing of the Beast God to a dinosaur-like creature.

#### Blessing of the Beast God

*These lizardmen are marked with elaborate crests containing striking colors and possess an instinctive kinship with other beasts who possess the same primal instincts.*

If the creature has a controlled mount with the Primal Instinct ability, it can have the mount take the Attack action once on each of the creature’s turns.

Additionally, while the creature or the creature it is mounted on is rampaging, attacks of the creature and the mount deal an additional 9 (2d8) damage on hit.

Finally, if the creature is rampaging, it may choose not to move on its turn if it is mounted, even if this would prevent it from being able to attack.

#### Blessing of the Blood God

*These hyper-aggressive lizardmen are marked with blood-red scales and infused with a ferocity that drives them to slaughter in their god’s name.*

While the creature is rampaging, its has advantage on attack rolls and deals additional 11 (2d10) damage on hit.

#### Blessing of the God of Fate

*These lizardmen are marked by the oldest of gods with pure white scales and are said to be destined for greatness as fate itself bends to their will.*

At the start of creature’s turns, it can choose to be under the effects of the *foresight* spell until the end of its next turn.

Once the creature uses this feature, it can't use it again until it finishes a long rest.

### Blessings of the Old Ones <br> Art Credit
* Thrakkus the Butcher - Nestor Ossandon Leal, Wizards of the Coast
* Raging Regisaur - Bayard Wu, Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### The Rampaging Condition
> Many creatures in this document have abilities that cause them to enter a rampage. Rampages last for one minute and have the following effect on a creature unless an ability states otherwise: <br>
> &#8226;  Any charmed or frightened effects on the creature are suspended.<br>
> &#8226; The creature must take the Attack action on each of its turns, targeting the nearest hostile creature it can see unless there are no creatures it can reach with an attack. <br>
> &#8226;  If no hostile creatures are within range of any of the creature’s attacks, it must use a Dash action to move toward the closest hostile creature it is aware of. <br>
> &#8226;  The creature can’t maintain concentration on spells or other effects.



<img
src='https://i.ibb.co/9shtDVn/card-na42-Z-art-crop.jpg'
style='position:absolute;top:-20px;right:-270px;width:920px;transform: scaleX(1)' />


 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:40px;top:0px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(270deg)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-390px;top:240px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(180deg)' />



\pagebreakNum

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-390px;top:120px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(195deg)' />

#### Blessing of the Hunter God

 *These lizardmen are marked with a brown spotted coloration to help them blend into the wilderness, and they possess superior predatory instincts that allow them to stalk prey through the thickest jungles.*

The creature has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide using foliage and may do so even if it is only lightly obscured. 

Additionally, the creature has advantage on Wisdom (Perception), Wisdom (Survival) checks and can make them as a bonus action. 

Finally, the creature can move through plants without being slowed, taking damage, or being grappled or restrained by them.

#### Blessing of the Protector God

*These lizardmen are marked with bony nobs and thick scales of a glittering silver color that deflect ranged attacks.*

While the creature isn’t rampaging, when a creature 10 or more feet away from it hits it with an attack or deals damage to it with a spell, the damage is halved.

#### Blessing of the River God

*These aquatic lizardmen are marked with sea-green hues, gills, webbed claws, and crocodilian jaws they can use to drag their foes to a watery grave.* <br>
The creature has a swim speed of 40 ft. and can breathe underwater. If the creature already has a swim speed, it is increased by 20 feet.

When the creature hits a creature with its bite attack, the target is grappled (escape DC equal to 8 + the creature’s Strength Modifier + Its Proficiency Bonus). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the creature can't bite another target.

\columnbreak

#### Blessing of the Stoic God

*These lizardmen are marked with yellow lines down their body that signify their impassive nature and level-headedness during combat.*

The creature adds +3 to its Wisdom, Charisma, and Intelligence saving throws and has resistance to psychic damage.

Additionally, its Primal Instinct feature is only triggered by it becoming charmed or frightened.

#### Blessing of the Sun God

*These energetic lizardmen are marked with the orange of the setting sun across their scales, and their sun god's power drives them to chase down their prey at alarming speeds.*

The creature has advantage on initiative rolls, and its speed is increased by 10 feet. If it would enter a rampage, it may use its reaction to move up to its speed toward any enemy it can see without provoking attacks of opportunity before its rampage begins.

#### Blessing of the Wind God

*These mystical lizardmen are marked with shimmering purple scales and possess primal wards that can sweep away enemy magics.*

The creature can cast *counterspell* once per day without any components, using Wisdom as its spellcasting ability. Its Primal Instinct ability is triggered when it casts the spell this way. (It can't cast the spell while rampaging.)

## Carnosaurs

In the dense jungles and vast plains where the Lizardmen thrive, few creatures strike as much awe and terror as the mighty Carnosaurs. These apex predators, with their fearsome presence and unmatched power, are both revered and feared, serving as powerful mounts for the most powerful lizardmen generals.

Carnosaurs are colossal reptilian beasts, standing several times taller than even the largest Lizardmen. Their muscular bodies, covered in thick, rugged scales, bear powerful limbs and a tail that acts both as a counterbalance and a weapon. Their maws are lined with razor-sharp teeth, capable of tearing apart even the toughest of foes. Among the various subspecies, some Carnosaurs sport varying amounts of feathers, adding a unique blend of ferocity and beauty to their appearance.

A Carnosaur on the battlefield is a sight of raw, primal power. These beasts are known for their bloody rampages, cutting through enemy lines with devastating ease. Their jaws and talons deliver grievous wounds, which, more often than not, result in the victim bleeding out over time. The scent of this spilled blood only intensifies the Carnosaur's bloodlust. 



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

They often enter feeding frenzies upon tasting it, making them all the more aggressive and insatiable when zeroing in on their bleeding prey.

Such is the might of the Carnosaurs that only the most influential Lizardmen commanders dare mount them for battle. Riding a Carnosaur is not about complete control but rather channeling its natural ferocity. Lizardmen riders, with their limited influence over these beasts, direct them towards the most optimal targets, letting the Carnosaur's instincts do the rest. 

It's a balance of guidance and unleashing raw power, a testament to the Lizardmen's symbiotic relationship with their environment.
Conclusion: Carnosaurs embody the raw essence of nature — unpredictable, unstoppable, and awe-inspiring. For the Lizardmen, these creatures are not just tools of war but symbols of primal might and their civilization's enduring bond with the ancient forces of the world. In every thunderous step and every devastating charge, Carnosaurs remind all of the primal force that the Lizardmen command.



<img src='https://i.ibb.co/pPyYL7z/Burning-Sun-s-Avatar-Ixalan-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:0px; width:900px;' />

  style='position:absolute;right:-260px;top:280px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(183deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

### Guldbloom's Terror 

There is one carnosaur of particular infamy known as Guldbloom's Terror. Named after the ill-fated explorer Jeffory Guldbloom, this creature is more than just a testament to the land's primal dangers. It's a living nightmare that has become the stuff of legends, told in hushed tones around campfires.

Jeffory Guldbloom, a renowned explorer and naturalist, arrived in the Lizardmen homeland with the noble intention of studying its diverse dinosaur fauna. However, during his expedition, his team came across a carnosaur unlike any they'd seen – an apex predator with unparalleled intelligence and power. Rather than being the observer, Guldbloom quickly found himself and his team the observed. One by one, members of his expedition vanished, leaving only signs of a fierce struggle. The group soon realized they were being hunted by this very carnosaur, leading to its grim title, Guldbloom's Terror.

\columnbreak

<br><br>

Unlike its kin, Guldbloom's Terror does not rely on sheer force but utilizes stealth and cunning, and its eyes burn with an uncanny intelligence. The creature's hunting technique sets it apart. Abandoning the carnosaur's usual straightforward assault, this beast specializes in ambush attacks. Its scaled hide allows it to blend seamlessly into the dense jungle, setting up perfect ambush points for its prey. What truly terrifies explorers and warriors alike is its methodical approach. Once it marks a target, Guldbloom's Terror hunts with chilling precision, using its environment to stalk, corner, and eventually strike with deadly efficiency.

Guldbloom's final notes, found abandoned near a destroyed campsite, spoke of the creature with a mix of fear and admiration. He wrote of its almost human-like ability to think, strategize, and execute plans. These notes serve as a grim reminder of the expedition's fate and a warning to all who dare tread in Guldbloom's Terror's territory.

___

>

If the target is a creature, it sustains two carnosaur wounds and is grappled (escape DC 18). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the carnosaur can't bite another target. At the end of each of the wounded creature's turns, it takes 2 (1d4) necrotic damage per carnosaur wound it has sustained. Carnosaur wounds can be healed if the creature regains 10 or more hit points or if a use of a healer's kit is expended on it. Alternatively, the wounded creature or another creature within 5 feet can make a DC 15 Wisdom (Medicine) check as an action, ending all carnosaur wounds on a success.
>
> ***Claws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 17 (2d8 + 8) slashing damage, or 28 (2d8 + 2d10 + 8) if the carnosaur is rampaging. If the target is a creature, it sustains a carnosaur wound as described in the Bite attack.
>
> ***Tail.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d8 + 8) bludgeoning damage, or 32 (3d8 + 2d10 + 8) if the carnosaur is rampaging.

If a creature fails the save by 5 or more (DC 13), it is also stunned. At the end of each of the stunned creature's turns, and each time it takes damage, it can make another Wisdom saving throw against the effect. The target has advantage on the saving throw if it's triggered by damage. On a success, the effect ends. <br><br>

##### Carnosaur Adventure Hooks
| d6  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Marshland Mutations:** A strange substance is leaking into the wetlands, causing carnosaurs to mutate into even more ferocious forms (which you can represent using Gifts of the Old Ones). The party must trace the source of this contamination and halt its spread.|
|  2  |**Escape From Texlacala:** During a diplomatic mission to the Lizardmen, negotiations turn sour. The party must escape the Lizardmen's capital while evading patrols of carnosaur-mounted warriors. |
|  3  |**Reptilian Special Forces:** A once tranquil rainforest has become a training ground for a Lizardmen faction specializing in guerrilla warfare who are being led by a powerful commander atop a carnosaur. The party must venture into this treacherous territory to put an end to their raids. |
|  4  |**Carnosaur Pursuit:** While the players are on a jungle expedition aboard an adventuring wagon, they find themselves being pursued by one or more carnosaurs who pose an overwhelming threat. They must race the wagon through the jungle as they attempt to escape their predatory pursuers. |
|  5  | **Trail of Terror:** Villages on the edge of the jungle have reported mysterious disappearances. Tracks resembling those of a carnosaur, but far more cunning and elusive, lead into the forest. The players are hired to investigate.|
|  6  | **Terror's Domain:** A rare herb, vital for a life-saving elixir, grows only in a particular clearing in the jungle. However, this clearing is now the territory of Guldbloom’s Terror. The players must stealthily retrieve the herb without alerting the beast.|

\columnbreak

### Carnosaur Tactics


Carnosaurs are apex predators, unafraid of any other creature. At the slightest hint of movement, they charge, using their claws to wound their target, followed by a powerful biting attack that sends them into a rampage. They use their tail attack to hit a secondary threat, but always prioritize hitting their primary prey with claw and bite attacks.

Despite their straightforward rampaging tendencies, carnosaurs have some tactical options. Their Blood Tracking ability allows them to pursue the most wounded prey in the area, bypassing the limitations of their rampaging condition. This is especially useful if the wounded target tries to flee. However, outside of this tactic, they still adhere to the standard rampage rules.

The carnosaur's innate lust for blood drives it to attack the most injured target with claw and bite attacks. If that creature manages to heal its wounds, the carnosaur promptly shifts its attention to the next nearest prey.

When lizardmen use carnosaurs as mounts, they shouldn't be treated as fully under the control of their rider unless that rider possesses the 'Blessing of the Beast God' from the lizardmen Blessings of the Old Ones list. A rider without this blessing is limited to guiding the carnosaur toward the most prominent target on the battlefield to unleash its wounding attacks. However, once the carnosaur begins to rampage, the rider loses all control, and the creature behaves as if it were wild.


#### Guldbloom's Terror 

Guldbloom's Terror exhibits unparalleled cunning compared to other carnosaurs. With its ambush ability and the Jungle Stalker trait, it patiently waits for the perfect moment to strike an unsuspecting target, often choosing the largest prey. Despite its sly nature, this creature is fearless and prioritizes kills that offer the most sustenance.
Guldbloom's Terror employs the same tactics as a standard carnosaur but doesn't risk entering into a rampage. It focuses on the most injured target it can detect, tearing it apart with cold precision rather than reckless rampaging.

This carnosaur also possesses legendary actions used in specific situations:

**Blood Tracking and Tenacious Will:** These are employed whenever something prevents the carnosaur from attacking a severely wounded target.

**Claw:** The carnosaur uses this attack when it's adjacent to the most injured prey or if it aims to start wounding a new creature.

**Bloody Roar:** This ability is used when the carnosaur can affect four or more targets with it or if it can impact at least two targets that are either concentrating on spells or flying beyond its reach. Possessing a natural instinct for magic detection, if Guldbloom's Terror senses a spell of seventh level or higher being concentrated upon, it will seek to disrupt it this way.

### Carnosaur Loot
The valuable items looted from carnosaur will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest the hide of a carnosaur. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Carnosaur Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Ceradons
Ceradons are imposing primeval beasts that roam the dense jungles inhabited by the lizardmen. These massive creatures have played a vital role in the history of the lizardmen, serving as powerful weapons of war. Their sheer size and strength make them formidable opponents on the battlefield, and their natural aggression makes them a fearsome sight to behold.

Ceradons are massive quadrupeds, covered in thick, leathery hide. They sport enormous bony plates along their backs, which provide natural armor and are often adorned with warpaint or other dedications to the lizardmen gods. Their most distinctive features are their large, downward-curving horns, capable of impaling and lifting even the largest foes. 

Ceradons are omnivores and opportunistic feeders, feasting on vegetation and small prey alike. However, they are also territorial and highly aggressive. They seldom retreat, often choosing to stand their ground and face foes head-on. Their primary mode of attack is charging, using their massive bulk to trample enemies or impale them with their horns. Their armored crests can deflect incoming attacks, making them challenging to land a counterattack against.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The lizardmen have long utilized ceradons in warfare. Skink crews equip these massive creatures with war howdahs, turning them into mobile fortresses. These howdahs often come equipped with giant blowpipes and ballistae that fire poisoned-tipped bolts, allowing the skinks to rain death upon their enemies from a relatively safe position. Occasionally, a howdah may be equipped with an engine of the gods, an ancient relic with arcane properties that skinks can channel to unleash devastating effects on the battlefield.

As ceradons age, they grow even larger and more powerful. The ancient ceradons are the most revered among their kind, their once fiery temper cooling with age. This makes them easier for skink crews to handle, and they are less prone to rampaging uncontrollably. Ancient ceradons are often equipped with the most elite and powerful howdahs, reserved for only the most critical battles.


<img
src='https://i.ibb.co/5YDZYX0/siege-horn-ceratops.jpg'
style='position:absolute;top:-0px;left:-0px;width:930px;transform: scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:310px; right:15px; width:900px; transform:rotate(13deg)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:370px; right:-150px; width:900px; transform:rotate(0deg)' />


\pagebreakNum

### The Thunderous One

This legendary ancient ceradon is said to be an avatar of the lizardmen storm god. It is a sacred beast, taller and more formidable than even its other ancient kin, and its presence is said to be an omen of great battles to come. Its scales are the color of a stormy sky, and its eyes crackle with the energy of a tempest. Unlike other ancient ceradons, the Thunderous One's temper has not cooled with age; instead, it rages like a storm, manifesting in thunderous effects that send shockwaves through enemy ranks.

In battle, the Thunderous One's steps echo with the sound of thunder, and its roars flash with claps of lightning. Those who incur its wrath not only face its primeval natural weapons but the divine lightning of its god. Bolts of this lightning rain down on the Thunderous One's foes and electrify those it tramples underfoot. 

\columnbreak

And should it enter a rampage, the Thunderous One's primal roar is said to be powerful to shatter armies and scatter dozens of foes before it. 

The howdahs mounted on the Thunderous One are the most powerful and sacred among the lizardmen, often adorned with religious icons and potent relics. They carry elite skink crews, who wield powerful weapons blessed by the lizardmen priests. These skinks, though humbled by their proximity to such a mighty beast, are the only ones with the experience and knowledge to guide the Thunderous One in battle.

In the heat of war, the Thunderous One becomes a force of nature, bringing the wrath of the storm god upon the enemies of the lizardmen. Its mere presence on the battlefield is a testament to the power of the lizardmen's gods and a sign that the storm god's will is manifesting through the actions of the lizardmen and their mighty ally, the Thunderous One.

___
___

> ***Cold Blooded.*** The ceradon has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Immutable Form.*** The ceradon is immune to any spell or effect that would alter its form.
>
> ***Impale.*** If the ceradon moves at least 20 feet straight toward a target and then hits it with a Gore attack on the same turn, the target takes an extra 13 (3d8) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, the ceradon impales the target on its horns, grappling it if it is a Large or smaller creature (escape DC 19). Until the grapple ends, the target is restrained, takes 20 (3d8 + 7) piercing damage at the start of each of the ceradon's turns, and the ceradon can't use its Gore attack.
>
> ***Primal Instinct (73 HP, Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the ceradon's hit points drop to 73 or fewer or it becomes charmed or frightened, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute.
>
> ***Territorial.*** The ceradon and any creature mounted on it have advantage on saving throws and checks against effects that would knock them prone or move them against their will. If any of them fail such a saving throw or check that they had advantage on, the ceradon enters a Rampage that lasts for one minute.  <br><br><br><br>
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The ceradon can make a Stomp attack against any number of creatures within 5 feet of it and then a Gore or Bite attack. It can forgo all of its Stomp attacks to use its Trample action.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 17 (3d6 + 7) piercing damage.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target not in the ceradon's space. *Hit:* 20 (3d8 + 7) piercing damage.
>
> ***Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 18 (2d10 + 7) bludgeoning damage. If the target is prone and in the same space as the ceradon, the stomp instead deals 29 (4d10 + 7) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ***Trample.*** The ceradon moves up to its speed in a straight line. During this move, it can attempt to enter Large or smaller creatures' spaces if it has moved at least 10 ft in a straight line beforehand. A creature whose space the ceradon would enter must succeed on a DC 19 Dexterity or Strength saving throw (the target's choice). On a failed save, the creature falls prone and takes 18 (2d10 + 7) bludgeoning damage, and the ceradon moves into its space. <br>On a successful Dexterity save, the target takes no damage, is not knocked prone, and is pushed 5 feet to the nearest space out of the ceradon's path. On a successful Strength save, the creature takes half damage, is not knocked prone, and the ceradon's movement ends.<br> If the ceradon remains in a prone creature's space, the creature is also restrained until it's no longer in the same space as the ceradon. While a creature is restrained in this way, it, or another creature within 5 feet of it, can make a DC 19 Strength check. On a success, the creature is pulled to an unoccupied space of its choice within 5 feet of the ceradon and is no longer restrained.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Armored Crest.*** When an attacker the ceradon can see makes an attack roll against the ceradon or a creature within 5 feet of it, the ceradon can impose disadvantage on the attack roll.



\pagebreakNum

### Howdahs
You can equip a dread saurus with one of the howdahs <br> described in the Howdah section earlier in this <br> document. This can include any of the howdah <Br> upgrades described in that section as well.

> _Huge monstrosity, unaligned_

>
> ***Stomp.*** _Melee Weapon Attack:_ +14 to hit, reach 5 ft. _Hit:_ 18 (2d10 + 7) bludgeoning damage. If the target is prone and in the same space as the ceradon, the stomp instead deals 29 (4d10+7) bludgeoning damage.

> ### Legendary Actions
>
> The ceradon can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The ceradon regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
>
> ***Check.*** The ceradon makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> ***Tenacious Will.*** If the ceradon is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated.
>
> ***Storm God's Judgement.*** The ceradon chooses a creature it is aware of within 300 feet of it that just took its turn and marks it for judgement. At the end of that creature's next turn, it must make a DC 21 Dexterity saving throw. The creature takes 16 (3d10) lightning damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. If the creature is restrained by the ceradon, it has vulnerability to this damage.
>
> ***Trample (Costs 2 Actions).*** The Ceradon uses its Trample ability.

##### Ceradon Adventure Hooks

| d6  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Raging Fire, Raging Beasts:** A dormant volcano in the lizardmen homeland suddenly erupts, sending molten lava and ash into the air. As though the eruption is not deadly enough, it also causes a nearby herd of ceradons to go on a wild stampede, threatening nearby settlements. The adventurers are called upon to protect these villages, divert the ceradon herd away from inhabited areas, and rescue any stranded villagers from the volcanic disaster. |
|  2  |**The Sunken Temple:** An ancient underwater temple has surfaced, rumored to be home to a legendary treasure. However, a fearsome ceradon guards the entrance, adorned with a howdah filled with elite skink warriors. The adventurers must carefully navigate the temple's traps and confront the ceradon and its crew to claim the treasure.|
|  3 | **Gift of the Gods:** A lizardmen tribe believes that the adventurers have been chosen by their gods to fulfill an ancient prophecy. They offer a tamed ceradon as a gift, complete with a howdah and skink crew. The adventurers must use their new allies to defend the lizardmen settlement from an impending demonic invasion.|

|  |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  4  |**Ceradon Siege**: A fortified city is under siege by lizardmen forces, and a massive ancient ceradon adorned with a war howdah is leading the assault. The adventurers must help the city's defenders repel the invasion, find a way to neutralize the ceradon, and uncover the reason behind the lizardmen's aggression.|
|  5 | **The Cursed Ceradon:** A powerful curse has befallen an ancient ceradon, making it a rampaging monster that terrorizes the jungle. The adventurers must seek the aid of a skink priest who knows how to lift the curse and restore the ceradon's original nature. They must battle dark magic, confront twisted spirits, and face the curse's origin to save the ceradon and the jungle it calls home.|
|  6  |**Storm God's Test:** The lizardmen believe the adventurers have been chosen by the storm god to undergo a trial. They must journey through the Thunderous One's storm-wracked home and prove themselves worthy by facing its challenges and surviving its wrath. Success will grant them the storm god's blessing and the favor of the lizardmen, but failure may have dire consequences.|

\pagebreakNum

### Ceradon Tactics

Ceradons are territorial, highly aggressive, and omnivorous creatures. While they don't actively hunt prey, they will readily attack anything within charging distance. In battle, a ceradon is resolute and acts primarily on instinct. It focuses on adversaries it perceives as the greatest threat, often choosing targets dealing significant damage or those of considerable size. However, it lacks the intelligence to realize the potential benefits of trampling multiple targets for increased damage output.

If a ceradon starts an encounter already in melee combat, it will retreat, even if doing so exposes itself to opportunity attacks. To defend against such attacks, it employs its Armoured Crest reaction. Following the retreat, it starts charging foes with its Trample action. The ceradon will follow this up with its Gore attack. While it can't gore a target right beneath it, it can trample over a target before circling back to Gore, often doing so with an advantage. Once an opponent is impaled on its horns, the ceradon shifts focus to trampling nearby threats. If it pins another creature under its feet, it will continue its stomp attacks while standing atop the pinned foe.

#### Ceradons With Howdahs

Ceradons equipped with a howdah can display tactical battle acumen under their rider's guidance. They frequently trample through dense clusters of enemies. Even if their Gore attack misses, if the ceradon pins two or more creatures beneath it, it remains stationary, concentrating on crushing them. 

The Armoured Crest reaction is used strategically, saved for countering potent spell attacks or deflecting high damage strikes, such as a rogue's sneak attack.

##### Ceradon Howdah Weapons 

Skinks usually man the ceradon's howdah. They employ long-range poison weapons integrated into the howdah to target enemies beyond the ceradon's reach, especially when the ceradon is stationary because it's pinning victims or it's pursuing elusive targets.

\columnbreak



#### The Thunderous One 

**Thunderous Wrath:** When the Thunderous One utilizes this ability, it repels adversaries not restrained by its feet or impaled on its horns, creating distance between it and its next target for an effective charge and Gore attack.

##### Thunderous One Legendary Actions

The Thunderous One utilizes its legendary actions in the following ways:

**Storm God's Judgement:** This legendary action is reserved for use against a creature impaled on the ceradon's horns or trapped beneath its feet. The Thunderous One instinctively employs this legendary action in this way, even without external guidance.

**Trample:** If there are no eligible targets for Storm God's Judgement, the Thunderous One defaults to this action. When under the guidance of more intelligent beings, it prefers to use this ability if it can potentially overrun more adversaries than those already pinned beneath it.

**Tenacious Will:** This action is invoked solely when its stomping and goring abilities are hindered or interrupted.


#### Engine of the Gods 

When operating a howdah equipped with an Engine of the Gods, understanding the sequence of how abilities should be used is crucial. Here's the recommended priority order:

1. Portent of Warding
2. Sacred Summon
3. Time Slows
4. Arcane Configuration
5. Burning Alignment
6. Healing Light

### Ceradon Loot
The valuable items looted from ceradons will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest the hide of a Ceradon. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Ceradon Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

##### Ceradon Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-10  | 2d4(5) 50gp Item |
|  11-15 | 2d6(7) 50gp Items | 
|  16-22 | 2d4(5) 100gp Items  |  
|  23-25 | 2d6(7) 100gp Items |  
|  26+ |  3d6(10) 100gp Items |  

##### Ancient Ceradon Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-8  | 2d4(5) 50gp Item |
|  9-11 | 2d6(7) 50gp Items | 
|  12-18 | 2d4(5) 100gp Items  |  
|  17-23 | 2d4(5) 200gp Items |  
|  24+ |  2d6(7) 200gp Items |  
 
##### The Thunderous One Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-8  | 3d6(10) 500gp Item |
|  9-11 | 3d6(10) 1,000gp Items | 
|  12-18 | 4d6(14) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  19-23 | 3d6(10) 2,000gp Items |  
|  24+ |  4d6(14) 2,000gp Items |

## Cold Bloods

These large raptors roam far and wide in large, rapacious packs tearing apart any warm-blooded creatures they come across. Cold bloods are known for their wild blood lust, vicious weaponry, and propensity for hunting in packs to bring down much larger prey.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

 Their sheer aggression is among their most dangerous traits, for wounded cold bloods do not flee but instead, become more recklessly aggressive. Even attempts to pacify or frighten a cold blood with magic will simply make it wilder and angrier.

___
___

> ## Cold Blood
> *Large beast, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 93 (11d10 + 33)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|18 (+4)|14 (+2)|16 (+3)|2 (-4)|8 (-1)|4 (-3)|
>___
> - **Skills** Perception +3
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 13
> - **Challenge** 3 (700 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&emsp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
>
> ***Cold Blooded.*** The cold blood has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Primal Instinct (31 HP, Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the cold blood’s hit points drop to 31 or lower, or it becomes charmed or frightened, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute. 
>
> ***Pack Tactics.*** The cold blood has advantage on an attack roll against a creature if at least one of the cold blood's allies is within 5 feet of the creature and the ally isn't incapacitated.
>
> ***Reptilian Brain*** When the cold blood fails an Intelligence or Wisdom saving throw, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The cold blood makes two attacks: one with its bite and one with its claws. 
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 13 (2d8 + 4) piercing damage.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 11 (2d6 + 4) Slashing damage.
>

<img
src='https://i.ibb.co/RGFbQxV/Marauding-Raptor-Core-Set-2020-Mt-G-Art.jpg'

\pagebreakNum





Cold bloods are extremely simple-minded, even by dinosaur standards. Though they have an instinctive ability to hunt in packs, their ability to assess complex situations and execute appropriate strategies is severely limited. Most cold bloods will pursue prey heedless of any danger which presents itself.

Despite their limited intelligence and aggressive natures, cold bloods can be successfully broken into mounts at scale. Because their territories range across many climates, they have been adopted for military use by multiple races. However, the lizardmen, who share their primordial jungle homes with the cold bloods, were the first to do so. Many of their saurian warriors are spawned with blessings that grant them a natural kinship with wild reptilian beasts and lend them to being natural cavalry fighters atop the vicious cold bloods. These mounted warriors make for devastating shock cavalry capable of running down and ripping apart even the hardiest of foes. 



### Horned Cold Bloods
These extremely rare raptors are thought to be near-extinct relatives of the cold bloods. They are only found deep in the primeval jungles where the lizardmen also make their home. Horned cold bloods don’t roam as far and wide as cold bloods and instead guard specific stretches of jungle they regard as their territory. Though horned cold bloods are significantly more intelligent than cold bloods, they are extremely protective of their turf and will fight to the death when attacking any intruders. As their name suggests, they are armed with boney horns, which they use to ram prey before finishing the kill with claws and teeth.

Horned cold bloods are prized mounts among the lizardmen. Their rarity, intelligence, and enhanced weaponry means they are ridden by only the most elite saurian soldiers and their generals. In battle, horned cold blood riders are implacable cavalry warriors, bowling down foes without giving an inch of ground.


\columnbreak

___
___

##### Cold Blood Adventure Hooks

| d6  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  |The players have been charged with venturing into a cold blood nest to retrieve eggs.|
|  2  |A wizard has resurrected a pack of long-dead cold bloods, which have broken free and now roam his lab. |
|  3  |The players have been tasked with capturing cold bloods to use as mounts. However, they soon find themselves in competition with lizardmen hunters.    |
|  4  |A cohort of lizardmen cold blood cavalry is moving through the countryside near their jungle home, sacking every minor warmblood settlement they find.|
|  5  |While lost in a deep jungle, the players find what appears to be a clear path out. The only catch is that it runs through horned cold blood territory.   |
|  6  | A saurian commander has gained control of a horned cold blood which he now uses as his savage steed to lead a lizardmen crusade against the warmblooded races.    |

### Cold Blood Tactics

Cold bloods are hyper-aggressive and have very low intelligence. Outside of making use of their Pack Tactics ability whenever possible, they don’t have any sophisticated combat tactics. They will simply try to gang up on and bring down the weakest prey they can spot. Allow them to fall for most ploys the party attempts, and let the players use their stupidity against them.

When used as mounts, their tactics will reflect that of the rider. However, the optimal strategy will still usually be to run down and gang up on vulnerable targets while hoping the cold blood doesn’t rapamge in the process.

#### Horned Cold Bloods

This variant should be played more intelligently and not fall for obvious ploys the same way cold bloods would. 

**Charge + Pact Tactics.** Whenever possible, horned cold bloods should use their Charge ability to target an enemy who has an ally within 5 feet of it, so they can combine it with their Pact Tactics. If they are mounted, this will be a non-issue.

### Cold Blood Loot
The valuable items looted from cold bloods will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest the hide of a cold blood. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

\columnbreak

#### Cold Blood Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Crox

Within the enigmatic lizardmen society, the crox stand as towering sentinels, dedicated protectors, and potent laborers. They are hulking creatures, towering above other lizardfolk. Their bodies are covered in armored scales, ranging in colors from deep blues to vivid greens and earthy browns. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Their heads resemble a blend of crocodile and lizard, featuring jaws capable of crushing stone and metal. Their powerful limbs, which end in deadly claws, enable them to move with surprising speed for their size.

___
___

> *Large monstrosity, lawful neutral*

>
> ***Maul.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 19 (4d6 + 5) bludgeoning damage.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The crox serve as the backbone of the lizardmen’s physical endeavors. In times of peace, they perform hard labor, assisting in the construction of temples, moving massive stone blocks, and dredging channels in the marshes. During war, they stand at the forefront of the Lizardfolk’s armies, swinging colossal weapons and smashing through enemy lines with their sheer might. 

While they are unmatched in physical strength, the Crox possess a simpler intellect than their smaller kin. As a result, they are often guided and directed by lizardmen leaders or skinks. Their loyalty to their kin is unwavering, and they carry out their tasks with a dedication that is both admirable and, at times, frightening.

### Sacred Crox

Some crox warriors are chosen to become something greater, something revered and sacred. These sacred crox, embody the very spirit of the gods the lizardmen worship. Not every crox has the potential to undergo this transformation. The process starts when skink shamen receive divine visions in their meditations, hinting at a particular crox that has been chosen by the gods. These crox are then taken to sacred groves, where they undergo rigorous rituals, awakening their latent divine power.

The Sacred Guardians are distinct from their Crox brethren. Their scales shimmer with an ethereal glow, reflecting hues that seem impossible in the natural world. Depending on the deity they are connected with, their eyes may burn with the cool blue of a serene lake, the fierce red of a blazing fire, or the deep green of the densest forest. And, while any crox could be spawned with unique markings displaying the blessings of one of their gods, the sacred crox are much more likely to carry these blessings, and their scales shine with the power they bestow.

If the target is a creature, it receives a Static Wound. For each Static Wound a creature has, its AC is lowered by 1, and it suffers a -1 penalty to all Constitution saving throws. This effect can't reduce a creature's AC below 1. At the end of the creature's turn, if it hasn't received a Static Wound since its last turn, it loses all Static Wounds.



<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

In battle, sacred crox are equipped with ornate gauntlets designed to channel their divine power into devesting blows. The strikes delivered with these weapons are not just capable of shattering bone, but unleashing radiant blasts of divine power. Sacred crox lumber into battle with these weapons, often using them to knuckle walk, before barrelling into foes and smashing them to a bloody pulp.

One group of sacred crox warriors have gained a special notoriety among enemies and allies alike. Known as the storm warriors, these crox have received special blessings from the lizardmen storm god. Their bodies are infused with the storm god's divine might, allowing them to channel lightning through their sacred gauntlets. Their blows statically charge their prey, leaving them with supernatural wounds that make them vulnerable to continued assaults. Storm warriors and their allies can use this tactic to quickly take down even the sturdiest foes with their divine onslaught.

### Crox Ancients
The crox ancients stand as living relics of the lizardfolk's past. These behemoths, blessed with extended lifespans, are easily distinguished by their colossal size, weathered scales, and the moss or lichen that grows on their forms, symbolizing their deep connection to the land.

Their longevity grants them a unique blend of instinctual war knowledge and experiential wisdom. Though they are not traditional thinkers, their primal understanding of combat and strategy makes them unparalleled tacticians. They lead not with complex orders, but with actions and guttural roars and shouts that their troops instinctively understand, creating a primal unity on the battlefield.

Crox ancients often wander the wilds, battling mighty beasts to test themselves as they grow stronger and wiser over the centuries. They have an uncanny knack for showing up when lizardmen forces are overwhelmed and in disarray. With their imposing aura of power and authority, they rally and lead whole lizardmen armies into battle where the crox ancient can unleash its titanic strength upon its hapless foes. Despite their ancient wisdom, they often lose themselves to bloodlust in battle, unleashing a primordial fury so terrible it scars the minds of those who witness it.

> ##### Optional  Reaction: Avenge Kindred
> If you're pairing your crox with skinks, you can give them the following reaction to help them work together:<br>
> ***Avenge Kindred.*** When a creature the crox can see deals damage to a skink within 30 feet of the crox that reduces its hit points to 0, the crox enters a rampage that lasts one minute and immediately moves up to its speed towards the creature and makes a melee weapon attack against it with advantage if it is within reach. 

##### Crox Adventure Hooks

| d8  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Crox Awakening:** Miners in a remote mountain region inadvertently awaken a group of crox from deep hibernation. These Crox, confused and aggressive, begin attacking nearby settlements. The party must find a way to either communicate with and calm the Crox or drive them away.|
|  2  |**The Crox Arena:** In a desert city, a cruel king hosts gladiatorial games where captured crox are pitted against other beasts and prisoners. The party could be captured and forced to fight, or perhaps they aim to free the enslaved crox and end the barbaric tradition. |
|  3  |**The Nimble & The Mighty:** Players travel through a lizardmen jungle, earning the ire of a skink patrol. Unable to face the players on their own, the skinks summon the aid of their mighty crox warriors to help them vanquish the intruders.  |
|  4  | **Guardian's Fall:** A group of sacred crox has been corrupted by a dark force, plunging nearby lizardmen regions into chaos. The party must investigate the source of this corruption and either save the guardians or put them to rest.|
|  5  |**Holy Rampage:** A divine conflict emerges between the lizardmen gods, who begin creating an unprecedented number of sacred crox to fight in their name. The different types of crox engage in holy rampages, each seeking to bring their god the most glory.     |
|  6  | **Guardians of the Storm:** An altar dedicated to an ancient storm god is believed to be causing a neverending hurricane threatening nearby port towns. Players who investigate the altar will find it guarded by zealous crox storm warriors. |
|  7  | **The Sacred Totem:** An artifact sacred to a crox ancient is stolen and sold to a black market. The enraged crox leads a rampaging army to retrieve it. The party can assist in the artifact's recovery, trace the black market's leaders, or exploit the chaos for their gain.  |
|  8  |**Primal Descent:** While the players explore the ruins of a far-flung and long-since-collapsed lizardmen civilization, they find the surviving lizardmen have descended into primal savagery and are led by crox ancients acting as brutal warlords.. |


\pagebreakNum


### Crox Tactics


Crox are inherently primal brutes, often attacking the nearest opponent out of pure instinct. These behemoths may fight using simple tactics and mindless aggression when on their own, but their true potential is unlocked when they are guided by smaller, more intelligent creatures, such as skinks.

In the hierarchy of Lizardmen, crox serve as formidable bodyguards and frontline soldiers. Although savage by nature, they display a surprising kinship with skinks. This unlikely alliance leads to the crox fiercely protecting skinks, even willing to risk their own lives to protect their allies unless instructed otherwise by a trusted skink companion.

The tactics described here are designed for use when crox are fighting alongside skinks but can be equally effective with other small, skirmishing humanoid units paired with crox.

Typically, the crox form the front line, advancing on the enemy. Directly behind them, the skinks utilize the crox's massive size as a protective wall. During their turn, the skinks maneuver through the crox to either engage any enemy units already in combat with the crox or, if the crox have yet to engage, to carry out ranged attacks.

Once their attacks are complete, the skinks retreat to safety behind the crox. They can also opt to use their bonus action to hide, leveraging the crox as cover if they possess the **Vanish** feature.

Should a crox go into a rampage, the skinks remain by its side until the battle appears lost or the crox can no longer provide sufficient cover.

#### Sacred Crox

Though sacred crox are more powerful than their ordinary kin and possess different types of weapons, they fight using the same tactics as typical crox. 

#### Blessings of the Old Ones
Crox with different blessings will follow mostly the same tactics as normal warriors, making small adjustments <br> to maximum their blessing's effect as nessecary. If <br> they have blessings that work with the rampage <Br> condition, there may be more circumstances <Br> in which they use their bite to try and enter <br> a rampage early.

\columnbreak


#### Crox Storm Warriors
Under the guidance of a more intelligent strategist, one or more storm warriors will concentrate their efforts on a single target, attempting to inflict as many Static Wounds as possible. Given that these wounds vanish after a round of not being hit by one of the storm warriors, the skink handlers encourage the crox to take substantial risks to maintain the infliction of these wounds on high-priority targets.

Any skinks concealed behind the crox will simultaneously concentrate their attacks on the now weakened target, utilizing javelins and poison. The weakened state of the target makes it more susceptible to these attacks, increasing the likelihood of successful hits and, thus, effective poisoning.


#### Crox Ancients
Despite their lack of conventional intelligence, crox ancients possess an almost instinctual sense of strategy and warfare. They can implement rudimentary tactics and issue near-animalistic commands to other crox, although they operate more like a pack of beasts than a unit of soldiers.
While crox ancients demonstrate greater intellect than their counterparts, they are most effective when paired with skinks, who serve as their advisors.

For optimal strategic placement, the crox ancients should be situated in the center of their group's formation. This position maximizes the benefit of its Aura of Endurance trait and its Coordinated Maul attack.

However, when a crox ancient begins to rampage, if there are no skinks nearby to maintain order, all crox in the vicinity lose any semblance of strategic cohesion.

### Crox Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from crox are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying. Though crox don't often collect these items themselves, other lizardmen often adorn them with bones, jewelry, and ornaments of precious metal for ceremonial purposes. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Crox Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Dread Saurus
These primeval titans are among the most feared <br> and powerful creatures that inhabit the jungles and <br> ruins of the lizardmen’s homeland. They are colossal quadrupedal, reptilian beasts, standing taller than even <br> the largest sauropods, and are protected by massive, armoured plates inscribed with ancient prophecies. 

Dread sauruses are revered as sacred beasts by the lizardmen, who keep them in mountainous temples where they receive offerings and sacrifices from skink priests. They are among the most valuable assets of the lizardmen army, as their ferocity and near-indestructibility make them devastating foes.


In the battlefield, the dread saurus can charge into enemy lines, crushing and trampling any foes in its path, and its powerful tail can sweep away entire squads of soldiers in a single stroke. Most deadly of all are its colossal, crocodilian jaws, capable of crushing and tearing the most formidable of foes into bloody shreds.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

***Skink Handlers and Howdahs.*** The dread saurus is often accompanied by skink handlers who can direct its attacks and use their own abilities to bolster its strength or weaken its enemies. These handlers can also provide healing and support to keep the creature fighting even in the face of overwhelming odds.

The skinks often direct the dread saurus from armored fortifications attached to its back, known as howdahs. They provide vital protection to the skink riders and are equipped with a variety of weapons, such as ballistae and giant blowpipes, which can be used to eliminate foes out of the dread saurus’s reach.

In addition to its combat capabilities, the dread saurus’s howdah is also used by the lizardmen as a means of transport. The howdah can carry additional supplies and equipment, making it an essential asset for military campaigns in the dense jungles of the lizardmen's homeland.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>
