> ## Dread Saurus
> *Gargantuan monstrosity, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 20 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 312 (16d20 + 144)
> - **Speed** 50 ft., swim 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|28 (+9)|8 (-1)|28 (+9)|4 (-3)|18 (+4)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Dex +5, Int +3, Charisma +5
> - **Skills** Intimidation +11, Perception +10
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 20
> - **Challenge** 18 (20,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +6
> ___
>
> ***Immutable Form.*** The dread saurus is immune to any spell or effect that would alter its form.
>
> ***Implacable.*** The dread saurus has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened, stunned, paralyzed, or incapacitated.
>
> ***Magic Resistance.*** The dread saurus has advantage on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.
>
> ***Primal Instinct (104 HP, Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the dread saurus’s hit points drop to 104 or lower, or it becomes charmed or frightened, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The dread saurus can use its Frightful Presence. It then makes a claw attack against any number of targets in a 10-foot-long and 20-foot-wide area that emanates from the dread saurus in a direction of its choice. It can replace one of the attacks with Bite or Crushing Jaws. It can then immediately make a tail attack against any number of targets in a 30-foot-long and 20-foot-wide area that emanates from the dread saurus in the opposite direction of its claw attacks. The dread saurus can't move between attacks.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 41 (5d12 + 9) piercing damage, and the target is grappled (escape DC 23). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the dread saurus can't bite another target.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target not grappled by the dread saurus. *Hit:* 23 (4d8 + 9) slashing damage.
>
> ***Tail.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 15 ft., one target not grappled by the dread saurus. *Hit:* 23 (4d8 + 9) bludgeoning damage, and the target must succeed on a DC 23 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
>
> ***Crushing Jaws.*** If the dread saurus has a target grappled with its bite attack, that target must make a DC 23 Strength saving throw or take 74 (10d12 + 9) piercing damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. If the target fails the saving throw by 10 or more (DC 13), the damage is doubled. If this damage reduces the target to 0 hit points, it dies.
>
>  ***Frightful Presence.*** Each creature of the dread saurus’s choice that is within 120 feet of the dread saurus and aware of it must succeed on a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw or become frightened for 1 minute. A creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If a creature’s saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the creature is immune to the dread saurus’s Frightful Presence for the next 24 hours.
>
> ***Obliterating Charge.*** The dread saurus moves up to 50 feet in a straight line and can move through the space of any Large or smaller creature. The first time it enters a creature's space during this move, it may make a claw attack against that creature.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Wounded Charge.*** When the dread saurus's hit points drop to 0 or it triggers its Primal Instinct ability, it can use its Obliterating Charge action. After using this action, the dread saurus dies if its hit points are 0.

***Artifacts of the Old Ones.*** Dread sauruses are often equipped with ancient relics believed to have been left behind by the inscrutable gods of the lizardmen. These artifacts are embedded in the dread saurus by its skink handlers and grant it arcane powers it can access at will. They may grant the dread saurus extra resilience, summon the spirits of dead warriors, or even allow it to channel the sun's energy through its body. When the divine powers of these artifacts are combined with the dread saurus’s primal might, it becomes a nigh unstoppable force of nature.

Dread sauruses equipped with these artifacts are considered avatars of the Old Ones' will. They are revered and protected by the lizardmen, not that they need much in the way of protection. Occasionally, particularly bold or mad relic seekers will attempt to hunt down these dread sauruses and pry the artifacts from their grasp. Such attempts nearly always end in disaster for the would-be treasure hunters.

\columnbreak

***The Dread Ripper.*** This dread saurus is believed to be the oldest and mightiest of its kind in existence. Its title stems from its record of shredding through any foe that has been foolish enough to stand against it. With its devastating natural weapons and near-limitless vitality, the Dread Ripper has singlehandedly shattered armies and leveled forts.

The Dread Ripper is thought to have walked the world since the time of the Old Ones, and the lizardmen revere it as a demi-god. In times of dire need, they will equip it with artifacts of the Old Ones and a war howdah crewed by only the worthiest of skinks. Despite its limited intelligence, the Dread Ripper possesses a near-supernatural aura of authority, and other lizardmen and jungle beasts will naturally flock to its side when it lumbers into battle.

\pagebreakNum

> - **Skills** Intimidation +13, Perception +12
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 22
> - **Challenge** 24 (62,00 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&ensp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +7
> ___
>
> ***Immutable Form.*** The dread saurus is immune to any spell or effect that would alter its form. 
>
> ***Implacable.*** If the dread saurus has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened, stunned, paralyzed, or incapacitated.
>
> ***Primal Instinct (182 HP, Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the dread saurus’s hit points drop to 182 or lower, or it becomes charmed or frightened, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute.

It then makes a claw attack against any number of targets in a 10 feet long and 20 feet wide area that emanates from the dread saurus in a direction of its choice. It can replace one of the attacks with Bite or Crushing Jaws, then it can immediately make a tail attack against any number of targets in a 30 feet long and 20 feet wide area that emanates from the dread saurus in the opposite direction of its claw attacks. The dread saurus can't move between attacks.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +16 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 48 (6d12 + 9) piercing damage, and the target is grappled (escape DC 24). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the dread saurus can't bite another target.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +16 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target not grappled by the dread saurus. *Hit:* 30 (6d8 + 9) Slashing damage.
>
> ***Tail.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +16 to hit, reach 15 ft., one target not grappled by the dread saurus. *Hit:* 30 (6d8 + 9) bludgeoning damage, and the target must succeed on a DC 24 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
>
> ***Crushing Jaws.***  One creature the dread saurus has grappled by its Bite attack must make a DC 24 Strength saving throw, taking 87 (12d12 + 9) piercing damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. If it fails the saving throw by 10 or more (DC 14), the damage is doubled. If this damage reduces the creature to 0 hit points, it dies.
>
>  ***Frightful Presence.*** Each creature of the dread saurus’s choice that is within 120 feet of the dread saurus and aware of it must succeed on a DC 19 Wisdom saving throw or become frightened for 1 minute. A creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If a creature’s saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the creature is immune to the dread saurus’s Frightful Presence for the next 24 hours.
>
> ***Obliterating Charge*** The dread saurus moves up to 50 feet in a straight line and can move through the space of any Large or smaller creature. The first time it enters a creature's space during this move, it may make a claw attack against that creature.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Wounded Charge.*** When the dread saurus's hit points drop to 0 or it triggers its Primal Instinct ability, it can use its Obliterating Charge action. After using this action, the dread saurus dies if its hit points are 0.
>
> ### Legendary Actions
> The dread saurian can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The dread saurian regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
> 
> **Check.** The dread saurian makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> **Gnaw.** A creature that just ended its turn and that is grappled by dread saurian's bite attack must make a DC 24 Strength saving throw, taking 39 (6d12) piercing damage on a failed save or half as much damage on a successful one. If it fails the saving throw by 10 or more (DC 14), the damage is doubled. If this damage reduces the creature to 0 hit points, it dies.
>
> **Mangle.** The dread saurian makes a Claw attack. A creature hit by the attack has its speed reduced by 20 feet until the end of its next turn.
>
> **Swat.** The dread saurian makes a Tail attack. If a creature fails the saving throw caused by the hit, it is pushed 30 feet away.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the dread saurian is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated.
>
> **Obliterating Charge (Costs 2 Actions)**. The dread saurian uses its Obliterating Charge.

##### Dread Saurus Adventure Hooks

| d6  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  |A lizardmen force has lost control of its dread saurus, which now rampages through the jungles unchecked.|
|  2  |A skink chieftain and crew atop a dread saurus howdah roams the coastline of their jungle home, sacking every fledgling port town they come across.    |
|  3  |In the face of an apocalyptic demon threat, the players have teamed up with a group of skinks and their dread saurus. From atop dread saurus’s howdah, they ride to face a demonic onslaught.|
|  4  |The players are sent to recover ancient artifacts that are currently being wielded by a dread saurus whose lair lies deep in ancient jungle ruins.    |
|  5  |The players stumble across an ancient tomb in the jungle cursed by an evil sorcerer. The curse has caused the long-dead lizardmen inside to reanimate as undead warriors, including a powerful dread saurus that must be slain to break the curse.    |
|  6  | The Dread Ripper has awoken from an ancient slumber and begun to rampage across the world, leading a crusading army of lizardmen in its wake who believe this to be a holy war.   |

### Dread Saurus Artifacts

The dread saurus can be equipped with a magical artifact that grants it additional abilities and increases its CR by 2.

#### Spirit Eye

*A mystic crystal is embedded in the dread saurus, which allows it to call forth primal warriors from ages past.*

At the start of its turn, the dread saurus can summon three specters in unoccupied spaces within 90 feet of it. The specters act immediately after the dread saurus on the same initiative count and fight until they are destroyed. They disappear after 1 minute or when the dread saurus dies. The specters summoned with this ability have the following changes:
* They are not affected by Sunlight Sensitivity.
* They have a melee spell attack instead of Life Drain. The attack has a +8 to hit, a reach of 5 feet, and targets one creature. On a hit, the attack deals 10 (3d6) force damage


#### Heart of Stone

*A large, eldritch stone is fused into the back of the dread saurus. The dread saurus can use the stone to draw the power of the earth into its body and become as unyielding as a mountain.*

At the end of the dread saurus's turn, if it has not moved on that turn and is standing on earth or stone, it gains a +3 bonus to AC, saving throws, and opposed checks. This ability can stack up to two times. The dread saurus loses all stacks if it moves or is forced to move.

While equipped with this artifact, the dread saurus's Primal Instinct ability is triggered only by it becoming charmed or frightened.

\columnbreak

#### Mantle of the Blazing Dawn 

*Strange golden patterns are etched across the dread saurus’s scales. As the beast charges, the markings flare and burn with divine radiance.*

Claw attacks made by the dread saurus when using its Obliterating Charge ability deal an additional 10 (3d6) fire damage and 10 (3d6) radiant damage on hit.


#### Primal Jaws

*The dread saurus’s teeth are etched with runes and gilded with rare metal to honor the most ancient of bestial gods. When the dread suarian crushes foes with its sacred jaws, it awakens a primal vigor in its allies.*

When the dread saurus uses its Crushing Jaws on a hostile creature, it and each ally within 100 feet of it gain 20 temporary hit points for the next minute. If the creature fails the saving throw against Crushing Jaws, they each gain 30 temporary hit points instead. If it fails by 10 or more, they each gain 40 temporary hit points instead.

#### Rebus of the Jungle

*Stange, magical, light-bending vines grow across the dread saurus and help mask its presence. These plants also help it to move through dense undergrowth undetected by its prey.*   

The dread saurus gets +11 to stealth checks and can move though plants without being slowed, taking damage, being grappled or restrained.

While dread saurus is lightly obscured, it is invisible to any creatures more then 10 feet away form it. If the dread saurus has a Howdah, the Howdah and the  Creatures inside of it gain this benefit as well

#### Figures of Dread

*The dread saurus wears a massive headdress lined with menacing statues, amplifying its already terrifying nature such that none can look upon it without experiencing mortal terror.*

The following ability replaces the dread saurus’s Frightful Presence:

 ***Dread Presence.*** Each creature of the dread saurus's choice within 120 feet that is aware of it must make a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw or become frightened for 1 minute. All creatures have disadvantage on the saving throw unless they are within 5 feet of an ally. Creatures normally immune to being frightened can still be affected, but have advantage on their saves. While frightened, the creature can only use its actions to Dash, Disengage, Dodge, Hide, or steel its resolve. A creature that uses its action to steel its resolve can repeat the saving throw, ending the effect on itself on a success. If a creature succeeds on the saving throw or the effect ends, it becomes immune to the dread saurus's Dread Presence for the next 24 hours.

### Howdahs
You can equip a dread saurus with one of the howdahs described in the Howdah section earlier in this document. This can include any of the howdah upgrades described in that section as well.

\pagebreakNum

### Dread Saurus Tactics
Dread sauruses are extremely belligerent and consistently seek to attack the largest group of enemies to inflict the most damage possible. They rarely consider going after the weakest targets. Their belligerence is so extreme that dread sauruses will usually fight to the death, rampaging to the very end.

#### Dread Saurus Ripper Tactics
The only real difference in tactics with a dread saurus ripper involves its legendary actions, which are used in the following circumstances:

* **Swat.** This is used when dread saurus has a creature in its mouth, and another creature is causing a large amount of damage that it wishes to be rid of.
* **Mangle.** If the dread saurus doesn't have any creature in its mouth and is attempting to catch fleeing prey, it will usually use this after using an obliterating charge.
* **Gnaw.** The dread saurus will use this action whenever possible, unless under the effects of a debilitating condition where it needs to use Tenacious Will.
* **Obliterating Charge.** The dread saurus uses this action to catch up with fleeing prey.

#### Dread Saurus Howdah Tactics
Dread sauruses on their own are generally not a significant threat to high-level parties as their dimwitted tactics and basic attacks can usually be countered by the many options players have at those levels. However, a howdah allows dread sauruses to be directed by intelligent creatures and should be filled with riders equipped with ranged attacks to create a more well-rounded threat.

The creatures in the howdah do not have to be tough, as the +5 to all saving throws, AC from cover, and damage reduction mean that the crew is well-defended as long as they stay within the structure. Their job should be to eliminate targets the dread saurus cannot reach.

\columnbreak

#### Dread Saurus Artifact Tactics
Dread saurus upgrades can allow it to present a higher-level and more complex challenge. Here are some basic tactics for several upgrades:
* **Spirit Eye.** This is similar to the howdah in that it compensates for the dread saurus’s weakness to ranged attacks and flying creatures. The summoned spirits can disrupt enemies the dread saurus can’t reach, and their intelligence allows them to do this in tactical ways that support the dread saurus.
* **Heart of Stone.** With this upgrade, it’s best to grab one target and chew it relentlessly, only moving if there’s no one left to attack. It works well in combination with a howdah.
* **Mantle of the Blazing Dawn** With this upgrade, the dread saurus should make an obliterating charge whenever it can hit three or more targets.
* **Jaws of the Savage** This upgrade works well in combination with a howdah or other minions.
* **Rebus of the Jungle** This upgrade allows the dread saurus to behave more like an ambush predator. When it’s not rampaging, the dread saurus’s strategy should be to lure targets into underbrush and darkness.
* **Figures of Dread** This upgrade does little to change the dread saurus’s tactics.

### Dread Saurus Art Credit
* Scaled Behemoth - Marco Nelor, Wizards of the Coast
* Enormous Baloth - Mark Tedin, Wizards of the Coast

### Dread Saurus Loot
The valuable items looted from dread sauruses will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them and whatever sacred items they’ve been adorned with. Harvesting a dread saurus’s body can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. Looting their adornments will usually involve an **Intelligence (Arcana)** or **Intelligence (Religion)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest its hide.

Players should be able to do both forms of harvesting at once using separate checks for most dread sauruses. 

If a dread saurus is equipped with an artifact, you can make a second roll for adornment loot. Alternatively, the players may recover a functional magic item from the artifact.

## Lord Krohc
*Mummified Mage-Priest Empowered By An Undying Spirit*<br>
**Habitat:** Jungle; **Treasure:** Arcane, Individual <br>

The sload mage-priests who survived the perilous eons since their creation by the Old Ones are mere shadows compared to the greatest of their kind who existed at the dawn of the world. The first sload mage-priests, forged by the Old Ones, were imbued with a supreme understanding of the universe, granting them power surpassed only by their creators. With a gesture, they could conjure hurricanes or rivers, weave spells to raise continents from the ocean floor, or plunge them back into the depths. Such was their mastery over the winds of magic.

Among them, the greatest was Lord Krohc, said to be the first of his kind to come into existence. No other being possessed a deeper understanding of the Old Ones' plans for the world, and only the most powerful beings could rival the might of this unparalleled servant. Yet even his immense power was tested during the Great Cataclysm that claimed the Old Ones and engulfed the world in chaos. Despite the combined efforts of the first generation of mage-priests, their powers were barely sufficient to fend off the evil born of that disaster. The salvation of the world came at a terrible cost: the loss of the greatest spellcasters to ever grace existence.

It is said that Lord Krohc was the last of his kind to fall. For years, he tirelessly held back an army of nightmares as vast as an ocean, casting spells with enough arcane might to topple mountains. Ultimately, his horrific foes overwhelmed him, tearing him apart. With his final breath, Lord Krohc unleashed a spell that swept away the remnants of his murderers, preserving what remained of the Old Ones' grand design.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

After the dust settled, the surviving servants of the Old Ones searched vigilantly for every scattered piece of the torn sage. They reunited his remains, binding them with sacred rites and placing them once more upon his stone palanquin. A golden death mask, inset with snow-white jewels for eyes, was laid upon the body of the mighty spellcaster so that he might continue to witness the flow of fate.

To this day, Lord Krohc's remains are housed within the most sacred temple of the Old Ones, guarded by lizardmen and revered by other sload mage-priests who offer tribute. Lord Krohc has become a symbol of the era when the Old Ones' plans remained untainted. Yet, Lord Krohc remains unconquerable, for his soul clings stubbornly to his withered corpse, refusing to depart this world. Those who visit the mage-priest's tomb feel the presence of his spirit, and some claim divine revelations, believing that Krohc still seeks to guide the children of the lost gods.

In the direst times—when the enemies of the Old Ones resurface or an omen reveals a fragment of the great plan demanding swift action—the sload mage-priests carry the mummified saint from his resting place, borne by his lizardfolk guardians. When roused, the spirit of Lord Krohc can draw celestial power to replicate the final spell he cast in life. Though its destructive force is minuscule when compared with the earthshaking incantation unleashed at the end of his life, it remains capable of grinding armies to dust once the venerable mage-priest's spirit completes his ritual.

> ### Traits
>
> ***Annul.*** If Lord Krohc fails a saving throw, he can choose to expend a Level of Power to succeed instead.
>
> ***Hypnotic Death Mask.*** Whenever any creature tries to attack Lord Krohc for the first time on a turn, the attacker must make a *Wisdom Saving Throw:* DC 22. <br>
> *Failure:* The creature is Charmed by Lord Krohc until the end of the turn, and it must choose a new target for its attack or the attack is wasted. <br>
> *Success:* The creature can attack Lord Krohc on this turn, but it has disadvantage on any saving throw it makes against Lord Krohc’s spells on its next turn.
>
> ***Telepathic Shroud.*** Lord Krohc is immune to any effect that would sense his emotions or read his thoughts, as well as to all Divination spells.
>
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Spatial Shift.*** Lord Krohc teleports up to 60 feet to a point he can see, one he can visualize, or one he can describe by stating distance and direction.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Eldritch Deliverance.*** Lord Krohc casts *Eldritch Deliverance*. His spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 22). The spell’s effective level is increased by 1 for each level of power the mage priest has.
>
> ***Arcane Blast.*** *Melee or Ranged Spell Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 150 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 18 (2d10 + 7) Force damage.
>
> ### Monstrous Actions
>
> Lord Krohc gains three additional actions in combat: Summmon Beacons, Essence Rend, and Resonating Pulse. Each action can be performed on its own initiative count (losing ties), separate from Lord Krohc’s own, if he is not Incapacitated. He can replace any action with Tenacious Will, and he can use Tenacious Will and Summmon Beacons even if Incapacitated.
>
> ***Summmon Beacons (Initiative Count 30).*** Lord Krohc creates four Eldritch Beacons in unoccupied spaces within 30 feet of himself. These Eldritch Beacons last until Initiative Count 30 of the next round. They act on their own turns on Initiative Count 1 and can only take the Infuse action on their turn.
>
> ***Essence Rend (Initiative Count 15).*** *Melee or Ranged Spell Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 150 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 29 (4d10 + 7) Necrotic damage, and the target’s soul is Rended for the next minute. While Rended, the creature takes 22 (4d10) Necrotic damage on Initiative Count 16 (losing ties) of each round. The effect ends early if the target regains 20 or more hit points in a single turn, or if a *Dispel Evil and Good* or *Greater Restoration* spell is cast on the target.
>
> ***Resonating Pulse (Initiative Count 5).*** *Melee or Ranged Spell Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 150 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 29 (4d10 + 7) Thunder damage, and the target is surrounded by rippling energy for the next minute. While surrounded by rippling energy, the creature is Restrained. If a creature other than Lord Krohc within 10 feet of the target casts a 1st-level or higher spell, the caster takes 22 (4d10) Thunder damage, and the rippling energy dissipates.
>
> ***Tenacious Will.*** If Lord Krohc is subject to an ongoing effect that allows a saving throw as an action or at the start or end of his turn, he can immediately make that save with advantage, ending the effect on a success.
>

</span>

\pagebreakNum


### Epic Battle: Indomitable Spirit
When Lord Krohc dies, you may choose to have his spirit rise from the remains. The spirit has the same stat block as Lord Krohc, except it has the following changes:

* The spirit loses the Golden Death Mask trait.
* The spirit is immune to all damage, as well as being Charmed, Exhausted, frightened, Grappled, Paralyzed, Petrified, Poisoned, Prone, or Restrained.
* The spirit can move through other creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. It takes 5 (1d10) Force damage, which ignores all damage immunities, if it ends its turn inside an object.
* Soul Struggle: Any creature that starts its turn within 60 feet of the spirit may choose to Struggle with the spirit. The Struggle lasts as long as the creature maintains concentration (as if concentrating on a spell) or until the spirit dies, up to a maximum of 10 minutes. While Struggling with the spirit, the creature ignores the spirit’s damage immunities. If the concentration breaks while the spirit is alive, the creature takes 27 (6d8) Force damage and is Dazed* until the end of its next turn.


Lord Krohc's spirit may perform an 8-hour ritual to his original body, fully restoring him, or providing a new body if the original no longer exists.

When Lord Krohc has access to this ability, both forms combined are treated as a CR 28 creature.

### Lord Krohc's Tactics

Lord Krohc’s primary objective in battle is to protect both himself and his Eldritch Beacons, ensuring he can gather enough power to unleash Eldritch Deliverance and annihilate his foes. He relies on his flight to stay mobile and out of reach of most threats.

**Eldritch Deliverance.** Lord Krohc casts Eldritch Deliverance every turn if possible. He prioritizes targeting the maximum number of enemies, but will focus specifically on creatures that suffer disadvantage on the saving throw due to his Hypnotic Death Mask trait.

**Summon Beacon.** The Eldritch Beacons are deliberately placed as far apart as possible to minimize the risk of being caught by area-of-effect spells. 

**Essence Rend.** This attack is used against a creature with the lowest AC that is not yet wounded.

**Resonating Pulse.** This attack targets a melee martial fighter that is unable to cast spells, making it as hard as possible to remove the resonating energy.

**Annul.** Used whenever there is something incapacitating Lord Krohc or preventing him from casting spells. 

#### Lord Krohc Epic Battle

Lord Krohc’s tactics remain relatively the same, except that he focuses on breaking the concentration of creatures Struggling with his spirit.

\columnbreak

#### New Spell: Eldritch Deliverance
*1st-level Evocation (Warlock)*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (a shard of meteorite)
- **Duration:** Instantaneous

You unleash a sudden pulse of eldritch energy at a point you can see within range. Each creature in a 5-foot-radius sphere centered on that point must make a Constitution saving throw. A creature takes 2d6 Force damage on a failed save, or half as much on a successful one.

***Using A Higher-Level Spell Slot.*** The damage increases by 2d6, the radius increases by 5 feet, and the range increases by 10 feet for each slot level above 1st.

##### Lord Krohc Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Echoes of the Final Spell.** An ancient battlefield, long buried beneath volcanic rock, suddenly surges with magic. Survivors whisper of glowing runes and ashstorms that move against the wind. Sload seers believe the residual energy of Lord Krohc’s final spell has become unstable, threatening to erupt again. The adventurers must descend into the heart of the ruined valley to anchor the fading echo and potentially face a remnant of Krohc's spirit.  |
|  2  |**The Lost Fragment.** An ancient vault believed lost since the Great Cataclysm has been discovered—within it lies a shard of Lord Krohc's original body, believed destroyed. This fragment pulses with arcane resonance, and several factions want it for themselves, claiming it holds spells lost to time. The adventurers may be tasked with retrieving or destroying the fragment before it falls into the wrong hands. |
|  3  |**The Echo War.** In an ancient memory vault beneath the temple-city, the adventurers activate a long-forgotten geomantic interface that replays the final hours of Lord Krohc’s last battle—complete with real enemies, magical terrain, and Lord Krohc himself reconstructed as a projection of war. But something goes wrong, and the simulation locks in place. Now fully aware, Krohc’s echo mistakes the adventurers for agents of chaos, and the party must survive his wrath in a gauntlet forged from the past. |
|  4  | **The Disturbed Slumber.** During a full celestial alignment, an opportunistic faction attempts to resurrect Lord Krohc entirely, believing they can return him to life to serve their own ends. The ritual succeeds only in disorienting and enraging Krohc's spirit. The adventurers must either subdue the rampaging entity or complete a different ritual to bring him peace once more.| 








\pagebreakNum


### Lord Krohc Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from sload mage-priests are the ancient relics they carry with them. However, some more macabre looters may harvest their remains for materials that hold some lingering power. Most carried valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** checks. At the DM's discretion, harvesting their bodies can be done using an **Intelligence (Medicine)** check. 

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Lord Krohc Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

##### Lord Krohc Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or <br> 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9 | 1 5,000gp Item |
|  10-12 | 1 10,000gp Items | 
|  13-19 | 1d4(2) 10,000gp Item  |  
|  20-24 | 1d4(2) 20,000gp Item |  
|  25+ | 1d6(3) 20,000gp Items |  

##### Lord Krohc: Indomitable Spirit Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or <br> 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9 | 1 50,000gp Item |
|  10-12 | 1 100,000gp Items | 
|  13-19 | 1d4(2) 100,000gp Item  |  
|  20-24 | 1d4(2) 200,000gp Item |  
|  25+ | 1d6(3) 200,000gp Items |

## The Last Defender

In the annals of lizardmen history, few heroes are revered as fervently as The Last Defender and his ferocious carnosaur steed, Grimlokk. The two are forever linked by their valor, their triumphs, and their unwavering commitment to their people.

The title of "The Last Defender" is not simply a moniker but a testament to this saurian general's valor and determination. As waves of ravenous demons beset a key lizardmen city, it was The Last Defender who rallied the last battalion of saurian warriors. Against overwhelming odds, they held their ground, ensuring the city's crucial artifacts were safeguarded and its legacy preserved.

Physically, The Last Defender is an imposing figure. Towering over other saurian, his scales bear the hues of deep azure mixed with streaks of golden yellow, symbolizing his celestial blessings. His age is marked by countless scars, each narrating tales of brutal confrontations, and his eyes shimmer with a wisdom and determination few can match.

A master tactician, The Last Defender is renowned for his skill in jungle warfare. He employs the dense foliage and treacherous terrain to stage deadly ambushes, leveraging the element of surprise to decimate his enemies. An aura of mystical defense surrounds him, granting divine protection to him and those nearby. In his hand, he wields a revered magical spear, said to be a gift from the gods.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

 Those unfortunate enough to be struck by it are tormented by nightmarish visions that fracture their very psyche. Complementing this is a gauntlet, worn on his left arm, capable of harnessing the sun's fury and releasing it in searing blasts upon his foes.

Grimlokk, The Last Defender’s loyal carnosaur, is a beast of nightmares. Larger and more ferocious than his kin, his dark scales are perfect for moving unseen through the dense jungles. While he possesses the raw power to tear enemies apart, he shows remarkable finesse in stalking and ambushing his prey, particularly targeting those already wounded to ensure their swift demise.

The bond between The Last Defender and Grimlokk transcends that of warrior and mount. Grimlokk obeys every command, every nuance, making their combat dance a seamless blend of precision and brutality. They function as extensions of one another, coordinating their attacks to maximize their impact on the battlefield.

Together, The Last Defender and Grimlokk symbolize the undying spirit of the lizardmen civilization. Their tales, spoken in hushed reverence by the skinks, serve as reminders of the sacrifices made and the relentless fight to ensure their race's survival in a world rife with threats. Their legacy is not just of victory, but of duty, resilience, and undying determination.

> ##  The Last Defender
> *Medium humanoid (saurian), lawful neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 18 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 287 (25d8+175)
> - **Speed** 30 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|24 (+7)|16 (+3)|24 (+7)|12 (+1)|24 (+7)|12 (+1)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Con +12, Charisma +6, Wis +12
> - **Skills** Athletics +12, Perception +12, Stealth +13
> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, frightened
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 22
> - **Languages** Draconic 
> - **Challenge** 15 (5,900 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +5
> ___
>
> ***Ambusher.*** The Last Defender has advantage on attack rolls against any creature he has surprised.
>
> ***Jungle Stalker.*** The Last Defender has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide using foliage and may do so even if he is only lightly obscured. Additionally, The Last Defender can move through plants without being slowed, taking damage, or being grappled or restrained by them.
>
> ***Primal Command.*** The Last Defender has a 30-foot aura of command. If The Last Defender is not rampaging, each other friendly rampaging creature of The Last Defender's choice has its rampaging condition suspended while within the aura.
>
> ***Spear Master.*** Spear attacks made by The Last Defender deal one extra die of their damage when he hits with them, has a range of 120 ft, gains the reach feature, and can gain the Versatile damage of the weapon while using one hand. (all included in the attack).
>
> ***Mounted Markman.*** While The Last Defender is mounted, he does not suffer disadvantage on ranged attacks due to a hostile creature being within 5 feet of him.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The Last Defender may use his Sacred Aura. He then makes four attacks, each one with a different weapon.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 14 (2d6 + 7) piercing damage. If The Last Defender rolls a 6 on one of the d6 damage dice with this attack, he may immediately make another bite attack against the target as a bonus action.
>
> ***Spear of Dread Visions (Magic Weapon).*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., or range 120 ft, one target. *Hit:* 17 (2d8 + 8) piercing damage. If the spear is thrown, it returns to The Last Defender's hand immediately after it is used to make a ranged attack. <Br> Once, during The Last Defender's turn, when it hits a creature with this attack, he can inflict the creature with a dread vision. At the end of each of this creature's turns, it takes 2 (1d4) psychic damage per vision it is suffering from. A creature can have multiple visions simultaneously, and if it is suffering from three or more visions, it is blinded and has disadvantage on Intelligence, Charisma, and Wisdom saving throws and checks until the visions are removed. <Br> Visions can be removed by the *remove curse* spell or any effect that can remove the blinded condition. A creature with visions or another creature within 5 feet can make a DC 15 Wisdom (Insight) check as an action, ending all visions on a success. <Br> A creature with Truesight cannot gain these visions, and all visions are removed if a creature gains Truesight. 
>
> ***Hand of Gods (Magic Weapon).*** *Ranged Spell Attack:* +12 to hit, range 100 ft., one target. *Hit:* 20 (4d10) Radiant damage.
>
> ***Tail Trip.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 16 (2d8 + 7) bludgeoning damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 20 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
>
> ***Sacred Aura (Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** The Last Defender summons a 30-foot mystical aura that lasts as long as he maintains concentration on it for up to 10 minutes (as if concentrating on a spell). Creatures of The Last Defender's choice in the aura's radius have advantage on all saving throws.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Sacred Wrath.*** In response to a creature under the effects of The Last Defender's Sacred Aura being damaged by another creature, The Last Defender can force the creature who inflicted the damage to make a DC 20 Charisma saving throw. That creature takes 16 (3d10) radiant damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one.
>

> ## Grimlokk
> _Huge monstrosity, unaligned_
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 18 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 287 (25d12 + 125)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|26 (+8)|16 (+3)|20 (+5)|6 (-2)|18 (+4)|12 (+1)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Str +13, Dex +8,  Int +3
> - **Skills** Perception +9, Stealth +13
> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, frightened
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 19
> - **Challenge** 15 (13,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +5
> ___
>
> ***Ambusher.*** Grimlokk has advantage on attack rolls against any creature it has surprised.
>
> ***Frightful Presence.*** Each creature of Grimlokk's choice that is within 120 feet of Grimlokk and aware of it must succeed on a DC 17 Wisdom saving throw or become frightened for 1 minute. A frightened creature repeats the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If a creature’s saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the creature is immune to Grimlokk's Frightful Presence for the next 24 hours.
>
> ***Jungle Stalker.*** Grimlokk has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide using foliage and may do so even if it is only lightly obscured. Additionally, Grimlokk can move through plants without being slowed, taking damage, or being grappled or restrained by them.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** Grimlokk has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Mangled Ligaments.*** If Grimlokk hits a creature that has three or more carnosaur wounds with a Bite or Claw attack, it mangles that creature. Until the mangled creature's carnosaur wounds are healed, its speed is halved, and it has disadvantage on attacks, checks, and saving throws that use Strength, Dexterity, or Constitution.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** Grimlokk can use its Frightful Presence. It then makes three attacks: one with its bite, one with its claws, and one with its tail. It can't make its tail attack against the same targets of its claw and bite attack.
>
> ***Bite.*** _Melee Weapon Attack:_ +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. _Hit:_ 34 (4d12 + 8) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it sustains two carnosaur wounds and is grappled (escape DC 18). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and Grimlokk can't bite another target. At the end of each of the wounded creature's turns, it takes 2 (1d4) necrotic damage per carnosaur wound it has sustained. Carnosaur wounds can be healed if the creature regains 10 or more hit points or if a use of a healer's kit is expended on it. Alternatively, the wounded creature or another creature within 5 feet can make a DC 15 Wisdom (Medicine) check as an action, ending all carnosaur wounds on a success.
>
> ***Claws.*** _Melee Weapon Attack:_ +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. _Hit:_ 17 (2d8 + 8) slashing damage. If the target is a creature, it sustains a carnosaur wound as described in the Bite attack.
>
> ***Tail.*** _Melee Weapon Attack:_ +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. _Hit:_ 21 (3d8 + 8) bludgeoning. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 21 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
>
> ### Bonus Action
>
> ***Blood Tracking.*** Grimlokk learns the exact location of each creature with a carnosaur wound within 300 feet of it. It then may move up to 25 feet toward a creature with a carnosaur wound without provoking attacks of opportunity.

### Epic Encounter: <Br> The Defender  & The Beast
If you wish to combine The Last Defender and Grimlokk in one encounter, you can grant them the following shared abilities. When using these abilities, treat them as a CR 25 creature for the purposes of  XP and encounter difficulty.

***Attuned to the Beast:*** When Grimlokk serves as The Last Defender's mount, The Last Defender can direct Grimlokk to take the Attack action once during each of The Last Defender's turns. If either Grimlokk or The Last Defender is reduced to 0 hit points, the other enters a Rampage state that lasts for one minute. While in this Rampage, they have advantage on attack rolls and deal an additional 11 (2d10) damage on successful hits.


#### Shared Legendary Actions
Grimlokk and The Last Defender possess a joint pool of 3 legendary actions when they are engaged in combat together, choosing from the options detailed below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time between both of them and only at the end of another creature's turn. They regain their expended legendary actions at the start of The Last Defender's turn. Should one of them fall, the other retains the ability to use these actions for the subsequent hour.

**Check.** Either Grimlokk or The Last Defender can perform a skill check that would ordinarily require an action.

**Movement.** Grimlokk or The Last Defender can move up to 30 feet without provoking attacks of opportunity. Should Grimlokk or The Last Defender come within 5 feet of each other during this movement, The Last Defender can instantly mount Grimlokk, provided he has a movement speed of 5ft or more. Additionally, he can opt to dismount Grimlokk at any time during this movement.

**Claw.** Grimlokk makes a claw attack.

**Spear.** The Last Defender makes an attack with the Spear of Dread Visions. If the attack hits a creature, that creature is afflicted with a vision (described in the attack description).

**Tenacious Will.** If either Grimlokk or The Last Defender is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. This legendary action can be used while incapacitated.

**Deadly Onslaught. (Costs 2 Actions)** Both Grimlokk and The Last Defender launch a wild barrage of attacks. Every creature within 5 feet of either of them must make a DC 20 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 13 (3d8) slashing damage and is inflicted with a carnosaur wound (as described in Grimlokk's Bite attack). However, if a creature that fails the save is within 5 feet of both The Last Defender and Grimlokk, it sustains two wounds.

**Roar of Reckoning. (Costs 2 Actions)** Grimlokk and The Last Defender simultaneously emit powerful, divine roars in twin 120-foot cones. Any creature other than Grimlokk and The Last Defender in the area of either cone must make a DC 20 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, it loses concentration, is knocked prone, and is inflicted with a vision (as described in The Last Defender's Spear of Dread Visions attack). If a creature is in the area of both cones, it receives two visions on a failed save.

##### The Last Defender Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Relic's Defender:** The players discover a map that points to a lost lizardmen relic of immense power. However, The Last Defender has been tasked to safeguard such relics from outsiders. As the players venture closer to the relic's location, they find themselves being stalked and ambushed by Grimlokk and his rider.|
|  2  |**The Eternal Last Stand:** The players come across ruins depicting ancient battles of The Last Defender and Grimlokk in a glorious last stand against hordes of demons. As they delve deeper, they unintentionally awaken these echoes, forcing them to relive the epic confrontations of the past either against or alongside The Last Defender.|
|  3 | **Jungle Pursuit:** The players are given a mission to track down a renegade mage who's taken refuge in the jungles. However, the mage has manipulated The Last Defender into believing the players are enemies. The players must evade the relentless pursuit of Grimlokk and his rider while trying to complete their mission.|
|  4  |**The Defender's Aid:** The players' jungle mission puts them in conflict with The Last Defender's duty. Yet, a larger threat emerges that jeopardizes both their objectives. The players must convince The Last Defender to join forces. Will he work with them or continue to see them as foes?|

### Last Defender <br> & Grimlokk Tactics

The Last Defender is a masterful warrior known for his strategic prowess. He often waits for the opportune moment to ambush foes and unleash his unique abilities. His loyal companion Grimlokk, follows his every command, creating potent synergy between their capabilities. 

**Wounds and Visions:** Both The Last Defender and Grimlokk have abilities that can stack damaging effects on enemies. These effects become highly debilitating at three stacks. In combat, prioritize stacking these effects.

**Sacred Wrath:** The Last Defender's Sacred Wrath reaction is reserved for adversaries with low Charisma, who will likely fail the saving throw.

**Blood Tracking:** This aids The Last Defender and Grimlokk in relentlessly pursuing wounded enemies. 

**Starting Turn:** Begin by stealthily approaching targets with The Last Defender mounted on Grimlokk. Once in position, Grimlokk should use its Frightful Presence and the defender should use his Sacred Aura. Focus the initial attacks on the most vulnerable enemy. If needed, leverage Grimlokk's ability to move with legendary actions to close distance. <Br><br>

**The Last Defender's Multiattack Sequence:**
* Initiate with a Tail Trip attack, followed by a Bite attack on the same target.
* Make the spear attack against the enemy with the most visions, even if the target is at a distance.
* For foes beyond Grimlokk's reach, such as flying enemies, use the Hand of Gods attack.



**Grimlokk's Multiattack Sequence:**
* Begin with a bite attack to grapple and restrain a target.
* Take advantage of the grappled foe by using a claw attack against it.
* After a bite and claw, it may make sense to carry a grappled target away from allies who could help it. Either way, Grimlokk should make a tail attack against another target if able.



**The Last Defender & Grimlokk's Legendary Actions:**
* **Movement:** The Last Defender can mount/dismount Grimlokk. Beyond closing this to close in on foes, they can also coordinate their movement to strategically split opponents. For example, Grimlokk could grapple a paladin with a protective aura and carry him away from the party, leaving them with The Last Defender.
* **Claw or Spear:** Choose which of these attacks to use based on which debuff stack (wounds or visions) is closer to 3 on the target.
* **Roar of Recking & Deadly Onslaught:** Use either of these abilities if you can affect four or more targets. These abilities are important ways to quickly stack wounds and visions on targets.

**Important Note:** Once either The Last Defender or Grimlokk falls in battle, the tactical strategies outlined above no longer apply.

\columnbreak

### Grimlokk & <br>The Last Defender Loot
Valuable items looted from Grimlokk will generally come from whatever can be harvested from it. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest the hide of a carnosaur. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

Because saurian are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from The Last Defender are the remains of the equipment he was using or valuables he was carrying. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** check. 

If you are combining Grimlokk and The Last Defender for a single epic boss battle, you can have them drop some truly valuable artifacts. These artifacts can be harvested or found the same way you find loot from The Last Defender. Though, you may change the checks to Intelligence (Religion) or Intelligence (Arcana) depending on the nature of the artifacts.

As an alternative to making any checks, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Grimlokk & <br>The Last Defender Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

##### Grimlokk Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-8  | 2d4(5) 200gp Item |
|  9-10 | 2d6(7) 200gp Items | 
|  11-17 | 3d6(10) 200gp Items  |  
|  18-23 | 4d6(14) 200gp Items |  
|  24+ |  5d6(17) 200gp Items |  
 
##### The Last Defender Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|

> These items are so rare they will typically deserve special descriptions and even lore background, giving them more relevance to the setting.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

## Lord Mazhalmundi
*Ancient Mage-Priest & Arbiter of The Great Plan*<br>
**Habitat:** Jungle; **Treasure:** Arcane, Individual <br>

Among the hoary mage-priests who, in ages past, wielded immense magical power to shape the world according to the designs of the Old Ones, none surpass Lord Mazhalmundi in age or arcane might. These ancient spellcasters were created to enact the will of godlike beings from beyond the stars—creatures who came to a primordial world and sought to mold it into a perfect design. Of those mage-priests who still survive into the present age, Mazhalmundi stands alone as the greatest. His power eclipses that of his peers, and his mind still carries echoes of the instructions handed down by the Old Ones themselves.

At the dawn of the world, Mazhalmundi was instructed in the arcane arts by the greatest of the mage-priests—those who spoke directly with the Old Ones themselves. So vast was his power that he could topple mountains and carve gaping rivers, shaping the world to the specifications of his divine creators. Yet, even with the mage-priests' masterful spellcraft and the Old Ones’ unmatched might, their vision for the world was never fulfilled. A calamity of unimaginable magnitude befell the planet, causing the Old Ones to vanish—whether slain in the cataclysm or abandoning their creations remains a mystery, even to the most learned mage-priests. Those who survived the initial devastation were soon assailed by abominations born from the chaos, which ravaged the land and plunged it into further discord.

In the wars that followed, all of the greatest mage-priests were lost in battle. Mazhalmundi and many of his kin had their minds tainted by the same chaos that had unmade the realms—their thoughts and calculations obscured by the disorder that flowed about them like a thick fog. Many entered deep trances in an effort to realign their minds and discern what must be done now that the Old Ones no longer guided their path.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

As the ages passed, Mazhalmundi remained motionless within his golden temple, hidden in the deepest jungles and protected by vigilant lizardmen who guarded the ancient sage for generations, awaiting his awakening.

In recent days, as the younger races arrogantly journey to forgotten lands to plunder and conquer, many relics left behind by the Old Ones have fallen into the hands of fools with no reverence or understanding of their true power. In his transcendent state, Mazhalmundi sensed this growing threat—and he rose once more. Over countless years, he had purged his mind of the corruption that hinders his brethren and reclaimed a portion of his former might. He has now determined what must be done to continue the Old Ones’ designs.

Mazhalmundi has concluded that before any new phase of the plan can begin, all species not crafted by the Old Ones must be eliminated—for their very existence disrupts the divine blueprint and halts the progress of its orderly fulfillment.

With these revelations fixed within the spellcaster’s unfathomable mind, his pronouncements echo psychically across the world. The oracles and lesser mage-priests of the lizardmen have heard his decree and gathered their forces to purge the mistakes that plague the world.

As for Mazhalmundi himself, he prepares to leave his sanctum, placing his great stone palanquin upon the fiercest of ceradon bound to his will. Atop this mighty beast, those he deems unworthy of the Old Ones' plan are swept aside with a wave of his amphibious hand, as the winds of magic bend to fuel his devastating incantations. Once Mazhalmundi passes judgment, no plea or protest can sway him—for the Great Work permits no clemency.

<img
src='https://i.postimg.cc/P5gH8bzC/ablb-5-dour-port-mage.jpg'
style='position:absolute;top:-480px;left:-105px;width:1100px;transform: rotate(-90deg) scaleX(-1)' />

\pagebreakNum

#### Epic Battle: Herald of The Great Plan
If you wish to make Mazhalmundi into a true threat worthy of providing the final battle to a campaign, you may have him ride atop his mighty ceradon steed **Zloq**. Together, they have a CR of 29.

\columnbreak

#### Devastation of Cities

You may give Mazhalmundi the Devastation of Cities set of actions described below; this increases his CR by 2.

<br>

> ### The Devastation of Cities
> **Cosmic Power.** When Mazhalmundi rolls initiative, he selects a point he can see and calls upon the Cosmic Powers to rend the earth. These entities, which possess an Intelligence of 24, act autonomously and always in Mazhalmundi’s best interest. For the next minute, or until Mazhalmundi dies, the Cosmic Powers remain active. While active, they are aware of the location of any creature within 120 feet of the chosen point.
>
> **Tremors - Occurs On Initiative Count 30 (Losing Ties).** The Cosmic Powers select a point within 300 feet of Mazhalmundi. A shockwave erupts from that point, forming a 90-foot-long, 30-foot-wide wave of upheaval that travels along the ground in a direction of the Powers’ choosing. The affected area becomes difficult terrain and begins to shake violently. Each creature of the Cosmic Powers’ choice standing on the ground in the area must succeed on a *Dexterity Saving Throw: DC 24*.
> 
> *Failure:* The creature is knocked Prone and cannot stand unless it uses all of its movement to do so on its next turn.
> 
> *Failure By 5+:* The creaure becomes buried, as the ground collapses beneath it. A buried creature is Restrained. Any creature, including the buried one, can use its action to free it with a DC 24 Strength check. This check has advantage if the creature attempting it has a Burrow speed.
>
> **Fissure - Occurs On Initiative Count 0 (Losing Ties).** 
The affected ground collapses, forming a fissure 40 feet deep and as wide as the original tremors. If the terrain is shallower than 40 feet, the fissure opens into whatever lies beneath (such as caverns or lava). Each creature and unattended object in the area must make a  *Dexterity Saving Throw: DC 24*.
>
>*Failure:* The creature falls Prone and into the fissure, taking 6d6 Bludgeoning damage, plus any damage from falling. 
>
> *Failure By 5+:* The creature is buried under rubble. A buried creature is Restrained. Any creature, including the buried one, can use its action to free it with a DC 24 Strength check, with advantage if the rescuer has a Burrow speed.

> ### Traits
>
> ***Adaptive Healing.*** At the end of Mazhalmundi turn, he chooses one damage type other than force. At the start of his next turn he regains 30 hit points. If Mazhalmundi takes 10 or more of the chosen damage type in a single turn, this trait doesn’t function at the start of his next turn. Mazhalmundi dies only if he starts his turn with 0 hit points and doesn’t regenerate.
>
> ***Harmonic Shield.*** Mazhalmundi has a shield with 3 charges. If he fails a saving throw, he can choose to spend a charge to succeed instead. At the start of his turn, the shield regains all of its charges. It can never have more than 3 charges at any time.
> A creature within 15 feet of Mazhalmundi can use its action or bonus action to make a DC 24 Intelligence (Arcana) check to attempt to disrupt the shield. <br>
> *Failure:* The creature takes 16 (3d10) Force damage.<br>
> *Failure by 10+:* The creature takes 33 (6d10) Force damage.<br>
> *Success:* Mazhalmundi loses 1 charge. <br>
> *Success by 10+:* Mazhalmundi loses 2 charges.<br>
>
> ***Mage Lord's Warding.*** Mazhalmundi can choose to ignore the effects of any of his own spells.
>
> ***Mind of Stone.*** Mazhalmundi’s concentration cannot be broken as a result of taking damage, and he can concentrate on two spells at once. If Mazhalmundi loses concentration, he loses concentration on both spells.
>
> ***Telepathic Shroud.*** Mazhalmundi is immune to any effect that would sense his emotions or read his thoughts, as well as to all Divination spells.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Cobara Mace.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (4d6 + 7) Bludgeoning damage plus 18 (4d8) Poison damage. At the end of the turn, each creature hit by this attack must make a *Constitution  Saving Throw:* DC 24  <br>
> *Failure:* The target is Poisoned. While Poisoned, the target can't concentrate on spells and all attunment to any magic items it has is suppressed . The target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of it's turns, ending the effect on a success. <br>
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** Mazhalmundi is a spellcaster. His spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 24, +15 to hit with spell attacks). 
>
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic* (9th level), *Disruptive Pulse** (8d8), *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/day:** *Eruption**, *Horrid Wilting***, *Maddening Darkness***, *Psychic Scream***, *Rebounding Blades**, *Storm of Renewal**, *Sunburst*, *Titanic Growth**, *Wrath of the Four Winds**
>
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Spacial Shift.*** Mazhalmundi teleports himself and the creature he is mounted on up to 60 feet to a point he can see. The destination can be a place he can visualize or one he can describe by stating distance and direction.
>
> ### Monstrous Actions
>
> Mazhalmundi gains two additional actions in combat: Cobra Strike and Siphon Fear. Each action can be performed on its own initiative count (losing ties), separate from Mazhalmundi's own, if he is not Incapacitated.
>
> ***Cobra Strike  (Initiative Count 20).*** Mazhalmundi or a creature he is mounted on moves up to 40 feet, and then Mazhalmundi makes an attack with his Cobara Mace.
>
> ***Mage-Lord's Magic (Initiative Count 10).*** Mazhalmundi casts a spell.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Counterspell.*** Mazhalmundi casts *Counterspell*, using Intelligence as his spellcasting ability.
>

> ### Traits
>
> ***Implacable.*** Zloq has advantage on saving throws against being Charmed, Frightened, Incapacitated, Stunned, or Paralyzed.
>
> ***Beast of the Mage Lord.*** Zloq can choose to ignore any of the effects of Mazhalmundi’s spells.
>
> ***Primal Revenge.*** When Mazhalmundi dies, Zloq enters a Rampage* that lasts for 1 minute.
>
> ***Massive Behemoth.*** Any creature mounted on Zloq benefits from half cover.
>
> ***Unstoppable.*** Zloq’s movement is unaffected by difficult terrain, and spells or other magical effects can neither reduce its speed nor move or teleport it against its will.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** Zloq makes a Stomp attack against any number of creatures within 5 feet of it, then makes either a Gore or Bite attack. It can forgo all of its Stomp attacks to instead use its Trample action.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target not in Zloq’s space. *Hit:* 24 (3d10 + 7) Piercing damage. If Zloq moves at least 20 feet straight toward the target before making this attack, the target takes an additional 16 (3d10) Piercing damage. If the target is a creature, Zloq impales it on its horns, grappling it if it is Large or smaller (escape DC 24). While grappled, the target is Restrained and takes 24 (3d10 + 7) Piercing damage at the start of each of Zloq’s turns—or 40 (6d10 + 7) if Zloq is Rampaging. Zloq cannot use its Gore attack while a creature is impaled this way.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 20 (3d8 + 7) Piercing damage.
>
> ***Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +15 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 20 (2d12 + 7) Bludgeoning damage. If the target is Prone and in the same space as Zloq, the attack instead deals 33 (4d12 + 7) Bludgeoning damage. If Zloq is Rampaging and the target is Prone, the attack is a critical hit, and the creature is paralyzed until the start of Zloq’s next turn.
>
> ***Trample.*** Zloq moves up to its speed in a straight line. During this movement, it can attempt to enter the spaces of Large or smaller creatures if it has moved at least 10 feet in a straight line beforehand. A creature whose space Zloq would enter must make a *Dexterity or Strength Saving Throw (target’s choice):* DC 24. <br>
> *Failure:* The creature falls Prone, takes 20 (2d12 + 7) Bludgeoning damage, and Zloq moves into its space. <br>
> *Successful Dexterity Save:* The creature takes no damage, is not knocked Prone, and is pushed 5 feet to the nearest space out of Zloq’s path. <br>
> *Successful Strength Save:* The creature takes half damage, is not knocked Prone, and Zloq’s movement ends. <br>
> If Zloq ends its movement in a Prone creature’s space, that creature is also Restrained until it is no longer in the same space as Zloq. While Restrained in this way, the creature, or another creature within 5 feet of it, can use an action to make a DC 24 Strength check. On a success, the Restrained creature is pulled to an unoccupied space of its choice within 5 feet of Zloq and is no longer Restrained.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Armoured Crest.*** *Trigger:* An attacker that Zloq can see makes an attack roll against it or a creature within 5 feet of it. <br>
> *Response:* Zloq imposes disadvantage on the attack roll.
>
> **New condition described on next page*

</span>

\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Mazhalmundi Tactics
Unlike typical spellcasters, Mazhalmundi leverages his cobra mace, immunity to his own spells, and mount Zloq to engage enemies up close. If Zloq dies, he falls back, keeping distance and striking lone vulnerable targets with his mace.

Mazhalmundi casts spells in the following priority order, adapting based on circumstances (e.g., enemy positions, statuses, or threats):

1. **Titanic Growth:** Cast on Zloq pre-combat if possible. (If he cannot cast it before combat starts, he prioritizes casting it immediately after Maddening Darkness.)
2. **Maddening Darkness:** Cast to maximize upfront damage before foes close in. Mazhalmundi is unaffected, so he centers it on himself for optimal coverage.
3. **Psychic Scream:** Prioritize hitting as many targets as possible.
4. **Eruption:** Target clusters of low-Dexterity or Stunned foes. Alternatively, cast into a fissure from The Ruination of Cities if 2+ creatures are trapped inside.
5. **Wrath of the Four Winds:** Use to shove low-Strength or Stunned targets back into Maddening Darkness/Eruption zones, or reposition them for Zloq's trample.
6. **Horrid Wilting:** Target as many low-Constitution foes as possible.
7. **Storm of Renewal:** Cast if Mazhalmundi or Zloq are Bloodied, or if either has suffered Poison, Blindness, or Paralysis.
8. **Sunburst:** Target groups of low-Constitution enemies.
9. **Rebounding Blades:** Hit clusters of low-Dexterity targets. Zloq can restrain foes in position to ensure they take returning blade damage.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

>  ##### New Condition: Rampaging
> The creature loses its free will as it enters a mindless rampage. Rampages last for up to one minute and have the following effect on a creature unless an ability states otherwise: 
> * Any Charmed or Frightened effects on the creature are suspended.
> * The creature can't cast spells or maintain concentration on spells or other effects.
> * On each of its turns, the creature must take the Attack action against the nearest hostile creature it can see within range. After attacking, it can't move for the rest of its turn. <br>
&emsp;If no targets are within range, it must move toward the nearest hostile creature it is aware of by the safest route. If it comes within range during this movement, it immediately takes the Attack action against it and then can’t move further. <br>
&emsp;If it is still not within range after moving, it must take the Dash action to continue approaching the nearest hostile creature.

<br>

#### Melee and Utility Actions:
* **Cobra Mace:** Use on unpoisoned targets, prioritizing spellcasters or those attuned to multiple powerful magic items.
* **Shift:** Reposition Zloq to trample multiple targets. Avoid teleporting if Zloq already has Restrained targets.
* **Adaptive Healing:** Each turn, select a damage type Mazhalmundi believes enemies cannot easily exploit against him.

#### Zloq Tactics
Zloq capitalizes on openings from Mazhalmundi's spells (e.g., Psychic Scream or Wrath of the Four Winds) by charging in to skewer foes on his horns, then dragging them into Maddening Darkness or Eruption zones for more damage.

#### The Ruination of Cities
These actions create fissures along the ground to block escaping foes (e.g., from Maddening Darkness) or drop Stunned targets into hazards.

##### Lord Mazhalmundi Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Unraveling Fault.** Lord Mazhalmundi has declared that a tectonic rift must be widened to realign continental convergence according to the Old Ones’ plan. To achieve this, he commands vast magical energies to rupture a heavily populated region, triggering earthquakes and awakening ancient volcanoes. As refugees flee and the land begins to shatter, the adventurers must uncover what cosmic threat he perceives and how to end the devastation.  |
|  2  |**Lost & Found.** A rising religious order worships the Old Ones in flawed, human-centric terms, and Mazhalmundi deems them a heretical threat to ancient world-runes buried beneath their temple. He commands their immediate extermination, and lizardfolk armies march in silence to fulfill his decree. |
|  3  |**The Star That Should Not Shine.** When a new celestial body appears in the sky, Mazhalmundi identifies it as a remnant of an ancient foe and begins constructing a titanic beacon to tear it from the heavens. Scholars and star-priests warn that disturbing the star could unravel planar stability, but the mage-priest remains unmoved. To prevent a cosmic rupture—or prove the star’s true purpose—the adventurers must act before the beacon ignites. |
|  4  | **The Fallen Void Vessel.** An enormous object crashes in the distant jungle—sleek, alien, and clearly artificial. Mazhalmundi declares it a remnant of the Old Ones' final departure and orders it sealed, even as explorers and empires rush to claim it. The adventurers may be hired by a faction to reach the wreck, discover its contents, or determine why the mage-priest wants it locked away.| 

### Lord Mazhalmundi Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from sload mage-priests are the ancient relics they carry with them. However, some more macabre looters may harvest their remains for materials that hold some lingering power. Most carried valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** checks. At the DM's discretion, harvesting their bodies can be done using an **Intelligence (Medicine)** check. 

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Lord Mazhalmundi Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Razorsaurs

Razorsaurs are naturally found in dense jungles, swamplands, and primordial river basins. Within the dense vegetation of their habitats, razorsaurs utilize their ability to launch spines to hunt prey or deter larger predators. These creatures are highly territorial and will almost never back down from a threat.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Skinks have learned how to keep razorsaurs in captivity for use as beasts of war. In combat, skink handlers guide the razorsaurs, relying on their natural aggression and defensive capabilities.

___
___
> ## Razorsaur
> *Large beast, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 17 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 90 (12d10 + 24)
> - **Speed** 40 ft, swim 40 ft
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|18 (+4)|18 (+4)|14 (+2)|3 (-4)|12 (+1)|4 (-3)|
>___
> - **Skills** Perception +7, Stealth +7
> - **Senses** Darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 17
> - **Challenge** 5 (1,800 XP) &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +3
> ___
>
> ***Cold Blooded.*** The razorsaur has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Primal Instinct (30 HP, Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the razorsaur’s hit points drop to 30 or lower, or it becomes charmed or frightened, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute.
>
> ***Spiked Hide.*** A creature that touches the razorsaur or misses it with a melee attack while within 5 feet of it takes 5 (2d4) piercing damage.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The razorsaur makes one bite attack and one claw attack, or it makes three attacks with its spikes.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 13 (2d8 + 4) piercing damage.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 10 (1d12 + 4) slashing damage.
>
> ***Spike.*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, range 100/200 ft., one target. *Hit:* 9 (2d4 + 4) piercing damage.
>
> ### Reactions 
>
> ***Instinctive Defence.*** When a creature moves towards the razorsaur and is within 15 feet of it, the razorsaur may make a Spike attack against it.
>

\pagebreakNum

When goaded by their handlers, razorsaurs unleash a hail of spines, turning them into deadly living ballistae.

These capabilities allow razorsaurs to play a critical role in lizardmen strategies. Forming the backbone of their ranged artillery, these creatures can quickly decimate infantry ranks with their barrage of spines. They are also adept at charging into enemy lines, using tooth and claw to wreak havoc.

#### Venomous Razorsaurs
This rare subspecies is prized by lizardmen for its poisonous spines. Found only in the deepest wilds, venomous razorsaurs are more patient than their kin, relying on their toxic spines to slowly sap the life from their prey before moving in for the kill. In war, their skink handlers use them to debilitate entire regiments of enemy soldiers, leaving them easy prey.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

\columnbreak



##### Razosaur Adventure Hooks
| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Isle of Spines:** An uncharted island has emerged from the sea, reportedly home to strange creatures, including feral razorsaurs. The players are hired to explore and document its flora, fauna, and any potential dangers. But soon after arriving, they come into conflict with lizardmen hunting parties here to capture razorsaurs for use as war beasts.|
|  2  |**Razorsaur Recruitment:** A military force battling lizardmen utilizing razorsaurs to great effect tasks the players with capturing razorsaurs of their own to see if they can be utilized in a similar fashion against the lizardmen, thus evening the balance of power. |
|  3  |**Razorsaur Pass:** In a war against the lizardmen, a crucial mountain pass serves as the only route for the players' allies to send reinforcements. However, lizardmen, using the natural high ground advantage and accompanied by razorsaurs, block the way. Players must clear the path and ensure safe passage. |
|  4  | **Spine Heist:**  A mysterious alchemist has found a way to extract a potent toxin from venomous razorsaur spines to use in the creation of devastating weapons for unscrupulous ends. The players must foil the alchemist's plan, which involves capturing venomous razorsaurs and extracting their deadly spines.|

A creature that has been hit by two or more attacks from weapons with Razorsaur Toxins this turn makes the saving throw with disadvantage. 
> 
> A poisoned creature repeats the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success or taking 9 (2d8) poison damage on a failure.

> ***Multiattack.*** The razorsaur makes one bite attack and one claw attack, or it makes three attacks with its spikes.

>

>

>
> ### Reactions 
>
> ***Instinctive Defence.*** When a creature moves towards the razorsaur and is within 15 feet of it, the razorsaur may make a Spike attack against it.
