### Razorsaur Tactics



&emsp;**In the Wild.** In their wetland homes, razorsaurs operate as ambush predators, typically stalking their prey through thick vegetation or by partially immersing themselves in water. Upon coming within 100 feet of their target, they release a barrage of spikes to incapacitate their prey. If the prey appears severely wounded and near death, the razorsaur moves in to deliver the fatal blow using its claws and teeth, preferring not to expend unnecessary spikes. However, if the prey still seems healthy and able to flee, the razorsaur often opts not to pursue, deeming the prey not worth the effort. Regardless of the situation, a razorsaur never flees, instead choosing to stand its ground defensively, flinging spikes at any aggressors. The razorsaur always uses its Instinctive Defense reaction when able.


**With Animal Handlers.** When directed by intelligent handlers, the razorsaur can act as a living artillery piece. Spiky Hide and Instinctive Defense provide it with a substantial deterrence against melee attackers, enabling its handlers to guide it towards enemy spellcasters and ranged attackers without facing less hindrance. Regardless of their training, razorsaurs always use their Instinctive Defense when possible, as their instincts cannot be fully suppressed.

#### Venomous Razorsaurs

&emsp;**In the Wild.** In the wild, venomous razorsaurs display a more patient approach than their ordinary counterparts. Their Razorsaur Toxins enable them to execute hit-and-run tactics, maintaining a safe distance while their poison takes effect. They always stay within firing range but avoid closing in until their prey has been significantly weakened and shows little sign of resistance. If a creature resists the toxins, the razorsaur will cease pursuit to avoid wasting spikes.

**With Animal Handlers.** When under the command of animal handlers, venomous razorsaurs serve as debuffers, spreading their poisonous spike attacks out among as many targets as possible. If one target is a greater threat, the razorsaur will allocate two of its spikes for that specific adversary to increase the odds of it being poisoned.

### Razorsaur Art Credit
* Tetzimoc, Primal Death - Zack Stella, Wizards of the Coast
* Bloodspore Thrinax - Ralph Horsley, Wizards of the Coast
* Hissing Iguanar - Brandon Kitkouski, Wizards of the Coast

### Razorsaur Loot
The valuable items looted from razorsaurs will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest the hide of a razorsaur. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Razorsaur Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

##### Razorsaur Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 5 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-7  | 1 5gp Item |
|  8-10 | 1d4(2) 5gp Items | 
|  11-16 | 1d4(2) 10gp Items  |  
|  17-22 | 1d6(3) 10gp Items |  
|  23+ |  2d4(5) 10gp Items |

## Saurian

Among the lizardmen civilization, the saurian are responsible for waging war and protecting their people. They are created for battle, emerging as fully formed adults from ancient spawning pools maintained by the lizardmen, ready to serve their purpose from the moment of their creation. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Though they don’t possess much in the way of standard intellectual prowess, saurian have an intuitive understanding of warfare and combat tactics, able to execute advanced tactical maneuvers that belie their slow-witted demeanor. 
___
___
> ## Saurian Warrior
> *Medium humanoid (saurian), lawful neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 16  (natural armor and shield)
> - **Hit Points** 75 (10d8 + 30)
> - **Speed** 30 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|18 (+4)|10 (+0)|16 (+3)|7 (-2)|16 (+3)|7 (-2)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Int +0, Charisma +0
> - **Skills** Athletics +6, Perception +5, Stealth +2
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 15
> - **Languages** Draconic 
> - **Challenge** 2 (700 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
>
> ***Cold Blooded.*** The saurian has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Primal Instinct (26 HP, Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the saurian’s hit points drop to 26 or lower, or it becomes charmed or frightened, it enters a rampage that lasts for one minute. 
>
> ***Titan's Grip.*** The saurian can wield two-handed weapons using one hand. 
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The saurian makes two attacks, each one with a different weapon.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 7 (1d6 + 4) piercing damage. If the saurian rolls a 6 on the d6 damage dice with the attack, it may immediately make another bite attack against the target as a bonus action and enter a rampage.
>
> ***Maul.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 11 (2d6 + 4) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ***Spiked Shield.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 7 (1d6 + 4) piercing damage.
>


<img
src='https://i.ibb.co/h9b5tcB/viashino-spearhunter.jpg'
style='position:absolute;top:-0px;left:-0px;width:820px;transform: scaleX(1)' />


<img
src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/rNOAD8A.png'
style='position:absolute;top:-60px;left:-100px;width:916px;transform: rotate(-13deg)' />



\pagebreakNum


<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The saurian combine the features of dinosaur and man, lumbering across the battlefield clad in iron-hard scales with powerful jaws capable of tearing into even the most heavily armored foes. Beyond their natural armaments, saurian wield massive stone weaponry and shields crafted from the hides of giant jungle beasts. These physical advantages, combined with cold, ruthless discipline and intuitive tactical know-how, make even a single rank-and-file saurian warrior more than a match for the typical soldier of another race.


Though the saurian are created to be disciplined and resolute soldiers, they still possess a bestial savagery in their hearts that harkens back to their primal ancestry. Saurian pushed to their limits in battle will throw off the pretense of restraint and enter a rampage, tearing into the nearest enemies they see, heedless of danger or even their orders. 

### Sacred Spawnings

It is believed that the gods of the ancient lizardmen watch over every saurian spawning, guiding their civilization along the great plan laid for the world at the dawn of time. Occasionally, a spawning will result in a batch of saurian bearing distinct colorations and abilities. These are thought to be blessings of the Old Ones used to create specialized warriors capable of aiding the lizardmen in unique ways. Through these blessed saurian, the divine will of the Old Ones is carried out, and the great plan is actualized.




\columnbreak

> ***Multiattack.*** The saurian makes two attacks, each one with a different weapon.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 16 (1d6 + 2d8 + 4) piercing damage. If the saurian rolls a 6 on the d6 damage dice with the attack, it may immediately make another bite attack against the target as a bonus action and enter a rampage.
>
> ***Maul.*** *Melee Weapon Attack*: +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 20 (2d6 + 2d8 + 4) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ***Spiked Shield.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 16 (1d6 + 2d8 + 4) piercing damage.
>

> Descriptions of the Blessings of the Old Ones can be found at the beginning of the creature's section of this document. You can apply one of them to the Sacred Saurian stat block to give it a specialized blessing, which increases its CR to 5.

### Temple Guard
While there are many types of unique saurian spawnings that can arise depending on the needs of the Old Ones, one variant carries a special reverence. Saurian of this spawning are known as the temple guard, and they possess an iron resolve and dedication to duty beyond the rest of their kind. These saurian are made to protect their sacred charges. These charges are most often venerable mage-priests of the lizardmen, but some temple guard may be assigned to protect particularly revered relics and divine location. 

Temple guards don ancient bones and armaments and perform their duties with supernatural discipline. They can stand motionless for centuries at a time, watching for the slightest sign of danger. Should such danger arise, they spring to action without a moment’s hesitation, shielding their charge from harm while ruthlessly striking down any threat. 

Such is their discipline that temple guards can rarely be phased by circumstances that would break the will of most. Even the innate savagery of their kind is kept in check so as to ensure the protection of their charge.

The most elite among the temple guard are referred to as the chamber guardians. Their service is reserved for the most sacred of sites and most venerable of mage-priests. Their guardianship is unsurpassed, for they are never surprised and possess martial capabilities beyond that of any other saurian soldiers. 

\columnbreak

### Saurian Commanders
Though the saurian have little to no say in the day-to-day governance of the lizardmen, which is left to the skinks, or the grand, long-term plans of their civilization, which is directed by the mage-priests, the saurian are the masters of leading wartime efforts. Saurian have no known maximum lifespan and grow more powerful with age. Those who’ve endured for centuries accrue enough experience to become leaders among their kind and, thus, the principal commanders for the lizardmen as a whole. These battle-worn saurian are referred to as scar commanders. 

The centuries of hard-won wisdom scar veterens have accrued not only makes them more potent combatants but also gives them the skills necessary to direct their kin to maximum effect. While a saurian general leads the battle, he can curb the primal instincts of the beasts and lizardmen under his command. However, should the commander himself succumb to his primal instincts, the rampage of his fellow beasts and lizardmen will be all the more frenzied as they follow his savage example.

The most ancient saurian generals have survived millennia of warfare and come to be known as elder bloods, the pinnacle of martial prowess and expertise amongst the lizardmen. Elder bloods can control the forces of the lizardmen as though they’re extensions of their own body and execute intricate battle tactics as intuitively as they wield their ancient weapons. To face an elder blood is to face a thousand years of martial mastery in the form of a single indomitable warrior.

\columnbreak

##### Saurian Adventure Hooks

| d8  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | The players are fleeing across an ancient bridge they must destroy to prevent pursuit from waves of incoming saurian.|
|  2  |The players are tasked with acquiring relics from scattered temples dedicated to ancient gods, but each relic is guarded by saurian blessed by their patron god. |
|  3  | Saurian warriors separated from their kind have succumbed to their primal nature and now rampage across the land.    |
|  4  |While traveling through an ancient icy cavern, the players accidentally release a cohort of saurian who’ve been trapped in ice for millenia.|
|  5  |The players have been tasked with recovering an ancient artifact being transported by a regiment of saurian temple guards.   |
|  6  | A mighty dragon has bound a contingent of chamber guardians to his will to use as his personal guard.    |
|  7  | A fledgling outpost on the coast of a newly discovered continent finds itself under siege by lizardmen led by a saurian scar commander.  |
|  8  |A saurian elder blood leads a ruthless campaign to raze all civilizations it views as corrupted by chaos. |

### Saurian Tactics
Saurian are direct and aggressive in their combat tactics and will usually fight to the death regardless of how dire their circumstances seem. They usually charge headlong into their foes, though they aren’t stupid about how they approach and won’t stumble into obvious traps or allow themselves to easily be put in a disadvantageous position. Saurian instinctively understand how to flank and outmaneuver foes, and they can usually pick out soft targets that need to be taken down first. 

Saurian are slightly stronger than other creatures at their CR because their Primal Instinct ability provides an exploitable weakness. As a DM, it’s important to communicate to the players when a saurian enters into a rampage what effect this appears to have on it. This way, clever players can use it to their advantage. 

#### Saurian Warriors
&emsp;**Bite.** Use this by default unless there is a commander ordering it not to. Because using bite has a chance to cause the saurian to rampage but also get another bite as a bonus action, the commander may order them to start using this attack if they are below 50 hit points and, therefore, close to rampaging anyway. Saurian will always use this in place of a shield attack if they’re rampaging.

**Maul.** Use this every turn as it is the most powerful attack.

**Shield.** Use this if a commander orders them to not use bites to avoid going into a rampage. Saurian won’t use this attack if they’re rampaging.

#### Sacred Saurian
These saurian follow mostly the same tactics as normal warriors. If they have blessings that work with the rampage condition, there may be more circumstances in which they use their bite to try and enter a rampage early.

#### Saurian Temple Guard
Temple guard, as their name implies, are designed to be bodyguards. They work especially well with spellcasters or other fragile ranged attackers. 

**Guardian’s Intervention.** Because this reaction reduces more damage if the saurian isn’t engaged in melee combat, temple guards will often stay near their charge rather than try to close in with players, even if they’re taking ranged fire.

**Sacred Duty.** It’s important to note this doesn’t stop Primal Instinct from triggering; it just suppresses the rampage condition while the temple guard is near its charge. Keep the guard close to its charge if you don’t want it running off after the nearest enemy.

#### Saurian Scar Veterens and Elder Bloods
While under the control of a saurian commander, other saurian will be much more tactical in how they attack and use their abilities. Saurian commanders have the following abilities they can use to influence the battle:

**Bite.** Because the saurian rolls 2d6 for damage, there is a much higher chance of this attack causing it to enter a rampage. The saurian will avoid using this attack unless it believes entering a rampage for the extra damage from its Primal Command aura will help its forces win the fight.

**Head Cracking Maul.** This is the saurian’s most damaging attack, and it will use it every turn, prioritizing spellcasters whenever it can.

**Puncturing Shield.** This attack is ideal against creatures with low strength and in situations where there aren’t too many enemies able to immediately make counterattacks against the saurian, so the loss of AC is manageable.

**Primal Command.** Because this aura suppresses the rampage condition, saurian within it will use their bite attacks as much as possible to try to score an extra bonus action bite without fear of succumbing to the effects of the rampage. 

**Tail Slam.** The knock-back from this attack makes it a useful escape tool or a way to push enemies apart to give other lizardmen a chance to gain better positioning.

### Saurian Loot
Because saurian are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Saurian Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.


##### Saurian Warrior Loot Table


| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-4  | 1 1gp Items |
|  5-6 | 1d6(3) 1gp Items | 
|  7-10 | 1 5gp Item  |  
|  11-17 | 1d4(2) 5gp Items |  
|  18+ |  1d4(2) 10gp Items |

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

## Skinks

While they are the smallest and frailest of the lizardmen, skinks are the glue that holds their society together. The saurian know little other than war and combat, so it falls to the skinks to serve as administrators, artisans, and any other form of skilled labor required by their empire. That is not to say they serve no purpose in war. While skinks are physically weak and skittish compared to the rest of their kind, they are cunning and nimble creatures capable of filling many specialized roles. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

***Warriors.*** Skinks' most common roles in combat are as mobile fighters who either ambush their foes or scamper into battle alongside larger allies. What they lack in brute force, they make up for with cunning tactics and poisonous weapons. These poisons are gathered from deadly jungle animals and used to debilitate foes in guerilla-style hit-and-run attacks. When fighting alongside larger creatures, skinks use these poisonous weapons to cripple their foes and make them easy prey for their deadly allies. 

___
___
> ## Skink Warrior
> *Medium humanoid (skink), lawful neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 17 (shield and natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 13 (3d8)
> - **Speed** 35 ft, swim 30 ft, climb 25 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|10 (0)|14 (+2)|10 (+0)|12 (+1)|14 (+2)|12 (+1)|
>___
> - **Skills** Animal Handling +4, Nature +3, Perception +4, Stealth +4, Survival +4,
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft. passive Perception 14
> - **Languages** Draconic 
> - **Challenge** 1/2 (100 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&emsp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
>
> ***Cold Blooded.*** The skink has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Evasion.*** When the Skink makes a Dexterity saving throw to reduce the damage of an effect by half, it
instead takes no damage on a success and only half damage on a failure.
>
> ***Hold Breath.*** The skink can hold its breath for 1 hour.
>
> ***Jungle Toxins.*** At the end of the turn, each creature hit by one or more weapons that inflict Jungle Toxins must succeed on a DC 13 Constitution saving throw or be poisoned for 1 hour. A creature that has been hit by two or more attacks from weapons with Jungle Toxins this turn makes the saving throw with disadvantage. The target repeats the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success or taking 5 (2d4) poison damage on a failure.
>
> ***Primeval Mask.*** The skink has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide using foliage or a creature larger than it and may do so even if it is only lightly obscured while hiding this way.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Javelin.*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 30/120 ft., one target. *Hit:* 5 (1d6 + 2) piercing damage, and the target is inflicted with Jungle Toxins.
>

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

***Skirmishers.*** Many skinks are trained as scouts and skirmishers who specialize in stealth and the use of poisonous blowguns. Their foes rarely see them for more than a moment before they disappear into the jungle canopy to prepare another crippling attack. Often times these skink skirmishers are sent ahead of a larger force to sow disorder among their foes before the larger lizardmen force smashes into their vulnerable prey.

___
___

>

\columnbreak

<Br>

***Behemoth Keepers.*** One of the more specialized roles some skinks assume is that of beast keepers. These skinks tend to larger reptilian beasts of war and are known as behemoth keepers. The reptilian monsters they tend to must be raised from birth if there is to be any chance of controlling them with any modicum of safety. The skinks form a bond with the beast they rear, which serves them well in combat, turning them into a fighting force greater than the sum of its parts.

\pagebreakNum

<br>

***Chieftains.*** Directing the skinks in day-to-day life as well as in combat are the chieftains. They are bolder than the typical skink and can drive their kind into a much more effective fighting force. A normally furtive and skittish group of skinks led by a chieftain can become a brutal strike force capable of rapidly bringing down foes typically outside their capabilities. The skink chieftains also serve as patrol leaders, heads of scouting parties, and battle coordinators for large lizardmen forces. They ensure battle plans are executed and pesky foes are eliminated as they conduct the war effort of the lizardmen army with brutal, calculating efficiency.

<img src='https://image.ibb.co/kC44nH/oF4JQBz.png' style='position:absolute; bottom:-00px; right:-300px; width:1200px; transform:scaleX(-1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>



\pagebreakNum



***Skink Priests.*** Though the mage priests are the highest-ranking members of their society, most of them spend too much time in isolated contemplation to effectively tend to the day-to-day operations of their civilization. This role is left to the skink priests, who serve as administrators and spiritual leaders to the lizardmen. Additionally, many skink priests are tasked with divining portents from many potential sources, whether they be celestial alignments, patterns in nature, or the murmurings of their mage priest masters. The priests use these portents to steer the course of their ancient civilization.

Though they possess a fraction of a mage priest's power, skink priests are still potent spellcasters, drawing on the power of the celestial heavens they study or the primal energies of their jungle home. When acting in the service of a mage priest, they can even serve as magical conduits for their master's power. They are also charged with operating the divine relics left behind by their gods, allowing them to unleash devastating power beyond their typical capabilities.

Priests who are in training or have failed to fully develop their powers nonetheless have some inate magical capabilities and can still serve as arcane vessels for their masters and, as such, are referred to as conduits. 


### Skink Conduit <Br> Lore of Magic Options 
Select one of the following lores or magic to determine a skink conduit's additional passive trait and spell list. <Br>
**New spells listed at the end of the document*

> #### Skink Conduit: Lore of Beasts
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Wild Heart.*** Whenever the skink targets only itself or one beast, monstrosity, giant, dragon, or fey with an Intelligence of 8 or less with a spell that requires concentration, it can choose for the spell to no longer require concentration. The spell ends early if the skink is incapacitated or uses this feature to alter another spell.  <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *guidance*, *primal savagery*, *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/Day:** *amber spear**, *pass without trace*,  *wild surge**



> #### Skink Conduit: Lore of Heavens
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Roiling Skies.*** Creatures flying 5 or more feet above a surface have disadvantage saving throws against spells cast by the skink, and the skink has advantage on spell attack rolls against them.  <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *guidance*, *shocking grasp*, *thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1Day:** *curse of the midnight wind**, *lighting strike**, *wind blast**

> - **Speed** 35 ft., swim 30 ft., climb 25 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|10 (0)|14 (+2)|12 (+1)|14 (+2)|14 (+2)|12 (+1)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Dex +4, Con +3, Int +4, Wis +4

> - **Languages** Draconic
> - **Challenge** 3 (700 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&ensp; **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
>
> ***Arcane Vessel.*** When a celestial, fiend, or dragon casts a spell on its turn within 100 feet of the skink and can see it, it can cast the spell as if it's in the skink's space instead of its own, using the skink's senses. The skink must be willing to allow this, and if the spell cast this way requires concentration, the skink can choose to maintain concentration on the spell in the other creature's place if the skink isn't already concentrating on a spell.
>
> ***Cold Blooded.*** The skink has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Eldritch Mind.*** The skink has advantage on Constitution saving throws it makes to maintain concentration spells.
>
> ***Evasion.*** When the skink makes a Dexterity saving throw to reduce the damage of an effect by half, it instead takes no damage on a success and only half damage on a failure.
>
> ***Hold Breath.*** The skink can hold its breath for 1 hour.
>
> ***Lore of Magic.*** The skink is specialized in one of the following lores of magic: Heavens or Beasts. The chosen lore determines one of its traits the spells it knows.
>
> ***Primeval Mask.*** The skink has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide using foliage or a creature larger than it and may do so even if it is only lightly obscured while hiding this way.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Quarterstaff.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +2 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 3 (1d6) bludgeoning damage, or 4 (1d8) bludgeoning damage if wielded with two hands.
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** The skink is a spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save DC 13, +4 to hit with spell attacks). The spells the skink knows depend on the lore of magic it has specialized in, as described in its Lore of Magic trait.

### Skink Adventures
The following table provides some ways to create adventures featuring these nimble lizardmen in your games:

##### Skink Adventures

| d10  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | While the players travel through a ruin-strewn jungle, a skink patrol spots them and moves in for an ambush.|
|  2  |The players come under attack by skink warriors that uses defensive tactics as it buys time for a larger lizardman force to arrive.  |
|  3  | The players seemingly manage to escape a jungle ruin, but as they flee through the wilderness, they are silently pursued by a group of skink skirmishers intent on ensuring they don’t make it out alive.     |
|  4  |A group of skink behemoth keepers is taking their newly trained monsters on excursions into nearby humanoid settlements, where they feed on livestock.    |
|  5  |A skink chieftain is launching raids against a fort to weaken its defenses in preparation for a larger lizardman attack.  |
|  6  |  A skink chieftain who’s lost all his larger lizardman forces seeks the players’ aid in helping his small skink force protect a sacred site from a demonic incursion.  |
|  7  | A skink priest has received a vision from the gods demanding the players be captured and ritually sacrificed to satisfy a coming prophecy.  |

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

|  |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  8  |Following the death of a mage priest, its skink priest attendants quickly begin losing their minds, taking control of the lizardmen it once ruled and leading them into a holy war to distract from their loss.   |
|  9  |While searching the abandoned jungle ruins for a lost relic, the players find themselves competing with a skink scout party seeking it as well.   |
|  10  | In the absence of mage priests, a group of isolated lizardmen have devolved into savagery. The remaining skinks seek the players' aid in culling their barbarous kin before they wreak havoc.  |

### Skink Tactics

Skinks generally keep their distance from the enemies, using their superior land, climb, and swim speeds to stay out of melee range. They generally work to debuff foes, and combo well with more powerful creatures who attack head on.

#### Jungle Toxins
Skinks rely on this ability for their own defense, as poisoned players will have a harder time hitting them with attacks or spotting them while they’re hidden. As such, they will try to poison as many enemies as possible.

#### Primeval Mask
This ability is vital for skinks initiating combat as they will never start a fight without the backup of more powerful creatures unless they can do so from an ambush.

#### Skink Warriors
These skinks have the fewest options for weaving in and out of combat, and so will rely on poisoning targets from a distance before engaging in melee. They will not close the gap with enemies who aren’t poisoned or in some way disabled.

#### Skink Skirmisher
Because these skinks have blowguns and the ability to hide every turn using their vanish ability, they will never engage in melee combat unless cornered.

#### Skink Behemoth Keeper
These skinks are usually found atop the howdas of larger creatures and will always make use of their Beast Bond ability to enhance their mount.


#### Skink Chieftain
These skinks lead their kind in battle. They have a few noteworthy abilities:

##### Coordinating Javelin
Chieftains will use this ability to help other skinks quickly land a second javelin strike against a chosen target, thereby increasing the likelihood of it failing its saving throw against the Jungle Toxins.

##### Stalking Cohort
This ability allows groups of skinks to focus fire poisoned targets. The skinks can pop out from hiding, launch volleys of ranges attacks, and then disappear again, quickly whittling down poisoned players.


\columnbreak

### Skink Priest Tactics

In battle, skinks can serve as the main spell casters or as supporters to more powerful spellcasters. Their traits make them resistant to magic, but they are still vulnerable to weapon attacks. Skink priests need some form of cover, be it foliage or a larger creature, to shield them from these threats. If several skink priests assist a more powerful spellcaster, they should space themselves out. This strategy grants the more powerful caster leading them better control over the battlefield.

#### Skink Lore of Beasts Tactics
Skinks adept in the lore of beasts excel when paired with a skirmishing group of fellow skinks and/or a larger beast, ideally both. Here's how their spells are optimally employed:

**Pass Without Trace.** This spell should be cast preemptively. If a skink enters combat without having cast this spell and there are three or more allies capable of hiding as a bonus action, the skink will still cast it during combat.

**Wild Surge & Aspect of the Beast.** The skink's Wild Heart trait enhances the effects of these spells. They are best cast on the largest beast it's allied with. If a skink priest possesses both spells, it should target the same beast with both. This ensures the additional attack granted by Aspect of the Beast benefits from the damage boost of Wild Surge.

**Call of the Pack.** The skink will cast this spell if it sees an ally within 5 feet of an enemy. The extra action from the spell allows the skink priest to either Dash or Disengage to safety or opt to Hide if the situation demands it.

**Amber Spear.** The skink should use this spell when it can hit 3 targets (or 2 targets with low Dexterity).

#### Skink Lore of Heavens Tactics

These skinks do best when positioned at elevated vantage points, such as atop cliffs, tall trees, or riding on flying beasts. They specialize in countering flying creatures, always prioritizing them with their spells. Here's how their spells are optimally employed:

**Lightning Strike.** This spell is most effective when cast on two or more creatures. If the skink priest has exhausted its major spells, it will resort to using Lightning Strike on single targets, prioritizing creatures with the lowest Dexterity.

**Curse of the Midnight Wind.** Ideally, this should be the skink priest's opening spell, especially if it can affect three or more targets.

**Wind Blast.** This spell is versatile and can be used to push one or more enemies into the effects of an Ice Storm or Comet's Call that the skink has previously cast.

**Ice Storm.** This is best used as the skink's second spell, especially if it can affect three or more targets.

**Comet's Call.** This spell acts as a defensive mechanism. If the skink is trapped in melee combat, it can cast this to potentially deter attackers. By leveraging its Evasion trait and superior Dexterity saving throw, the skink can usually survive the comet's impact, whereas its assailants might suffer harsher effects. However, the skink will still attempt to move out of the impact zone if possible. The skink prioritizes casting this after Curse of the Midnight Wind and Ice Storm.


\pagebreakNum

### Skink Loot
Because skinks are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most dropped or hidden valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** checks. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Skink Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Sload Mage-Priests
*Ancient Arcane Masters & Stewards of The Great Plan*<br>
**Habitat:** Jungle; **Treasure:** Arcane, Individual <br>
Deep within the primeval jungles lie hidden temples from a bygone age, their enigmatic structures standing as relics of a lost era. At the heart of these strange edifices are vast chambers, where the air is thick with humidity and hums with sorcerous power. In the center of each chamber floats a massive, bloated creature of immense mystic might—surpassed only by the gods themselves. These spellcasters are the sload mage-priests: ancient, amphibian beings who manipulate magic as effortlessly as mortals breathe.

Seated upon golden palanquins that hover gently above the ground, sustained solely by their esoteric thoughts, these beings wield unparalleled arcane power. Their bulbous eyes perceive the strands of magic weaving through the world, and with elegant gestures of their multi-jointed fingers, they draw arcane energy to themselves like rivers rushing to the sea. With such vast magical reserves, a sload mage-priest can unleash spells of devastating magnitude—storms of fire that consume cities, entire armies turned to stone in a flash of light, or thoughts amplified into overwhelming cacophonies that shatter the minds of even the most astute wizards.

The powers of the sload mage-priests vary among their kind. Some wield terrifying defenses, ignoring blades and arrows as if they were illusions, while others are nearly unkillable, regenerating severed limbs and knitting gaping wounds within seconds. Certain mage-priests can silence enemy spellcasters with a mere gesture, unraveling incantations and rendering their magic impotent.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The sload are said to have been created by a race of godlike beings who sought to reshape the world according to their grand design. The sload were crafted to aid in this monumental undertaking. Guided by their divine makers, they shifted continents, altered planetary orbits, and nurtured species deemed worthy while purging those found unfit. But this great plan was never completed. A cataclysm—unwittingly triggered by the very designs of their creators—plunged the world into chaos. When the dust settled, the gods were gone, and the mightiest sload mage-priests—those with the deepest knowledge of the plan—had perished.

Those who remain are the last of their kind. Most dwell in their humid chambers in deep meditation, so profound that they might be mistaken for dead. In truth, their minds are anything but idle—they traverse time and space, contemplating the fragmented instructions left by their vanished masters. These trances can last lifetimes without interruption. When a sload mage-priest finally stirs, it is often because they believe they have uncovered a fragment of the great plan and now intend to act upon it.

Guarded by vast cohorts of lizardmen who revere them as living saints of the Old Gods, mage-priests command unwavering loyalty. When they proclaim what must be done to fulfill the divine vision, their cold-blooded followers act without hesitation. Whether these actions stem from true divine insight or a desperate search for purpose is irrelevant—when a sload mage-priest acts with conviction, few forces in the world can stand in their way.


<img src='https://i.postimg.cc/zfkQ9jhw/Lilysplash-Mentor.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-120px; right:-120px; width:1100px; transform:scalex(-1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:175px; right:60px; width:900px; transform:rotate(10deg)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:250px; right:0px; width:900px; transform:rotate(0deg)' />


\pagebreakNum

### Disciplines of The Old Ones
A sload mage-priest can be granted any of the following traits to reflect its age and power. Younger mage-priests typically have one trait, while the eldest mage-priests may have as many as four. Each trait granted increases its CR by 2. 

#### Becalming Cogitation
The mage-priest can cast *Dampen Magic* at will.

#### Harrowing Scrutiny
At the start of the mage-priest’s turn, it unleashes an aura of otherworldly authority. Each hostile creature within 120 feet of it must succeed on a *DC 20 Wisdom Saving Throw.* <br>
*Failure.* The creature is Frightened until the start of the mage-priest’s next turn. While Frightened this way, the creature can cast only cantrips. <br>
*Failure by 10 or More.* The creature is Paralyzed while Frightened. <br>
*Success.* The creature becomes immune to Harrowing Scrutiny for 24 hours.

#### Harmonic Convergence
At the end of its turn, the mage-priest may begin a ritual drawing on the winds of magic. While the ritual is active, it has advantage on spell attack rolls, and creatures have disadvantage on saving throws against its spells. A creature within 15 feet can use an action or bonus action to make a DC 20 Intelligence (Arcana) check to disrupt the ritual.

*Failure.* The creature takes 22 (4d10) Force damage. <br>
*Failure by 5 or More.* The creature takes 33 (6d10) Force damage. <br>
*Success.* The ritual ends. <br>
*Success by 5 or More.* The ritual ends, and the creature channels some of the energy. The next spell of 1st level or higher it casts before the end of its next turn is cast as if using a slot 1 level higher.

#### Higher State of Consciousness
The mage-priest can move through creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. It takes 5 (1d10) Force damage if it ends its turn inside an object. It has resistance to Bludgeoning, Piercing, and Slashing damage. If the mage-priest takes 30 or more damage from spells on a turn, it loses this trait until the start of its next turn.

#### Focus on Mystery
On initiative count 30 of the first round of combat (losing initiative ties), the mage-priest casts *storm of magic*. This casting doesn’t require concentration and ends only if the mage-priest chooses to end it or dies.


#### Soul of Stone
The mage-priest’s concentration on spells can’t be broken as a result of taking damage.


\columnbreak

#### Transcendent Healing
Choose one damage type other than Force. The mage-priest regains 20 hit points at the start of its turn. If the mage-priest takes 20 or more damage of the chosen damage type before its next turn, this regeneration doesn’t function on its next turn. The mage-priest only dies if it starts its turn with 0 hit points and doesn’t regenerate.

#### Unfathomable Presence
The mage-priest has resistance to damage from spells. If it takes 30 or more Bludgeoning, Piercing, or Slashing damage on a turn, it loses this trait until the start of its next turn.

> ### Traits
>
> ***Limited Hover.*** The mage-priest can’t hover more than 15 feet above a surface or across a liquid that can't support it.
>
> ***Telepathic Shroud.*** The mage-priest is immune to any effect that would sense its emotions or read its thoughts, as well as to all Divination spells.
>
> ***Lore of Magic.*** The mage-priest is specialized in one of the following lores of magic: Beast, Death, Fire, Heavens, High Magic, Life, Light, Metal, or Shadow. The chosen lore determines one of its traits and the spells it knows, and it may cast the spells without material components.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** The mage-priest is a spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Intelligence (spell save DC 20, +12 to hit with spell attacks). The spells the mage-priest knows depend on its Lore of Magic trait.
>

### Sload Mage-Priest <br> Lore of Magic Options 
Select one of the following lores or magic to determine a sload mage-priest's additional passive trait and spell list. <Br>
**New or Revised Spell Found at End of Document*<Br>
***Spell Found in Xanathar's Guide to Everything*<Br>

<br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Beasts
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Wild Heart.*** Whenever the mage-priest targets only itself or one Beast, Monstrosity, Giant, Dragon, or Fey with an Intelligence of 8 or less with a spell that requires concentration, it can choose for the spell to no longer require concentration. The spell ends early if the mage-priest is Incapacitated or uses this feature to alter another spell. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Amber Spear**, *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Primal Savagery*** (4d10), *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/day:** *Bestial Spirit** (6th level), *Summon Stampede**, *Titanic Growth**, *Unleash the Beast**  <br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Death
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Life Leech.*** Whenever a non-undead, non-construct creature fails a saving throw against or is hit by a spell attack from one of the mage-priest’s spells of 1st level or higher, the mage-priest gets a +1 to its spell save DC and spell attack rolls for the next minute. It can only gain this bonus once per casting of a spell, and this bonus can stack up to 3 times (+3). <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Chill Touch (4d6)*, *Commune*, *Crippling Pain**, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/day:** *Circle of Death* (7th level), *Horrid Wilting***, *Horrifying Laughter**, *Purple Sun** <br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Fire
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Kindleflame.*** When the mage-priest deals fire damage to a creature with a spell, it gains a burn then takes 1d4 Fire damage for each burn it has. The creature loses all burns after one minute of not receiving one. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Fire Bolt* (4d10), *Fireball*, *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy* <br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Heavens
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Roiling Skies.*** Creatures flying 5 or more feet above a surface have disadvantage saving throws against spells cast by the mage-priest, and the mage-priest has advantage on spell attack rolls against them. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Guidance*, *Lightning Strike**, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Shocking Grasp* (4d8), *Thaumaturgy* <br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of High Magic
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Contemplations.*** When the mage-priest casts a spell that it has not Contemplated, it can choose to Contemplate the next spell it casts. A spell that is Contemplated has its effective level increased by 2. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Disruptive Pulse** (4d8), *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Soul Quench**, *Thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/day:** *Flames of the Phoenix**, *Power Word: Stun**, *Psychic Scream***, *Rays of Magic**  <br>



\pagebreakNum

>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Lifebloom.*** When the mage-priest casts a spell, the mage-priest or a creature it can see within 60 feet of it regains hit points equal to 3 + the spell’s level. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Gift of Life** (3rd level), *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy*, *Thorn Whip* (4d6) <br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Light
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Guiding Light.*** Whenever the mage-priest casts a spell of 1st level or higher that targets or affects other creatures, it can choose any number of those creatures and have them automatically succeed on any saving throws against the spell, and they take no damage from the spell if they would normally take half damage on a successful save. Additionally, the chosen creatures gain advantage on Wisdom and Charisma saving throws until the start of the mage-priest’s next turn. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Dazzling Light**, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Sacred Flame* (4d8), *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/day:** *Crown of Stars***, *Divine Judgment**, *Sunbeam*, *Sunburst*  <br>

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Metal
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Metalshifting.*** Creatures made of metal or wearing heavy or medium metal armor have disadvantage saving throws against spells cast by the mage-priest, and the mage-priest has advantage on spell attack rolls against them. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Acid Splash (4d6, deals Fire damage instead of Acid)*, *Commune*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Slow*, *Thaumaturgy* <br>
> **1/day:** *Final Transmutation**, *Plague of Rust** (6th level), *Rebounding Blades**, *Weapon of Power (doesn’t require concentration)**   <br>

\columnbreak

> #### Sload Mage-Priest: Lore of Shadow
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Shadow Paths.*** When the mage-priest casts a spell of 1st level or higher, it may use teleportation to swap places with a willing Medium creature within 30 feet of it that it can see. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At Will:** *Commune*, *Creeping Strike (4d8)*, *Detect Magic*, *Dispel Magic*, *Guidance*, *Mage Hand*, *Prestidigitation*, *Scrying*, *Sending*, *Thaumaturgy*, *Withering Resolve** <br>
> **1/day:** *Path of Shadows**, *Pit of Shadows**, *Maddening Darkness***, *Weird** <br>



### Sload Mage-Priest Tactics
Sload mage-priests are powerful spellcasters who excel when supported by minions, allowing them to maintain distance while unleashing devastating spells or providing support to their allies. Their tactics vary based on their assigned Lore of Magic, with each lore granting four primary spells. If their enemies remain undefeated—or are not close to defeat—after expending these spells, mage-priests should retreat.

#### Lore of Beasts
Mage-priests of the Lore of Beasts excel when paired with a powerful creature (e.g., Carnosaur, Ancient Ceradon) that they can buff. Pre-battle preparation is critical.

* **Summon Stampede:** Cast before combat or on the first turn, targeting the largest enemy group.
* **Titanic Growth:** Cast before combat or on the second turn, using Wild Heart to enhance a powerful creature.
* **Amber Spear:** Cast while *Summon Stampede* and *Titanic Growth* are active, targeting low-Dexterity enemies.
* **Unleash the Beast:** Use to punish a creature engaging the mage-priest in melee, attacking and then retreating.


#### Lore of Death
Mage-priests of the Lore of Death wait to use powerful spells until their Leech Life trait has been maximized.

* **Horrifying Laughter:** Target a low-Wisdom creature surrounded by allies to trigger Leech Life.
* **Circle of Death (7th level):** Cast to hit multiple low-Constitution targets.
* **Horrid Wilting:** Cast to hit multiple low-Constitution targets.
* **Purple Sun:** Cast after losing concentration on *Horrifying Laughter* or when *Leech Life* is maximized.
* *Crippling Pain* on targets reliant on bonus actions.




\pagebreakNum

#### Lore of Fire
Mage-priests of the Lore of Fire prioritize targets affected by their Kindle Flame trait, casting spells in this order:
* **1st:** Incendiary Cloud
* **2nd:** Meteor Swarm
* **3rd:** Burning Bolts
* **4th:** Fire Storm
* **5th:** Fireball

#### Lore of Heavens
Mage-priests of the Lore of Heavens position themselves on elevated vantage points (e.g., cliffs, tall trees) and specialize in countering flying creatures.

* **Storm of Vengeance:** Cast to create a barrier between the mage-priest and enemies, using effects in this order:
    * **Thunder:** Stuns targets to ensure they fail saving throws against other spells.
    * **Lightning:** Targets stunned or low-Dexterity enemies.
    * **Hail:** Deals additional damage.
    * **Rain:** Deals additional damage.
* **Wrath of the Four Winds:** Pushes targets back into Storm of Vengeance, prioritizing collisions with other creatures or walls (low-Dexterity targets) to enhance *Chain Lightning* effects.
* **Chain Lightning:** Targets the largest group of low-Dexterity creatures.
* **Whirlwind:** Used if concentration on Storm of Vengeance is lost, Restraining as many targets as possible.
* **Lightning Bolt:** Targets the largest group of low-Dexterity creatures.



#### Lore of High Magic
Mage-priests of High Magic focus on isolating and eliminating targets, using Contemplations to enhance spells.

* **Psychic Scream:** Targets as many enemies as possible, stunning them for follow-up spells.
* **Flames of the Phoenix:** Targets multiple low-Dexterity or stunned enemies; revive the Phoenix if it can hit three or more targets.
* **Power Word: Stun:** Targets a creature with low hit points and low Constitution.
* **Rays of Magic:** Use Contemplations to upcast, targeting as follows:
    * **Fire:** Low-health or stunned targets.
    * **Beasts:** Ranged fighters to move allies into melee or to escape.
    * **Metal:** Highly mobile targets (e.g., monks, rogues).
    * **Light:** Targets that hide to avoid damage (e.g., rogues).
    * **Life:** Pushes melee fighters away.
    * **Heavens:** Targets next to another enemy.
    * **Shadows:** Martial fighters.
    * **Death:** Low-health or Stunned targets.
* **Soul Quench**: Targets creatures concentrating on spells.

#### Lore of Life
Mage-priests of the Lore of Life manipulate the battlefield by controlling enemy movement and reviving or healing allies.

\columnbreak

* **Dwellers Below:** Cast to affect as many targets as possible, centered on the mage-priest, forcing enemies to navigate difficult terrain to reach them.
* **Warden’s Wrath:** Pulls creatures that escapes *Dwellers Below* back into its area.
* **Regrowth:** Cast when two or more allies have died to revive them.
* **Storm of Renewal:** Cast after losing concentration on *Dwellers Below*.
* **Gift of Life:** Cast on the most valuable ally or the mage-priest themselves.

#### Lore of Light
Mage-priests of the Lore of Light try to group enemies and allies together to maximize the Guiding Light trait’s potency.
* **Crown of Stars:** Cast before combat or when unable to hit four or more targets with other spells.
* **Sunburst:** Best when affecting four or more creatures (enemies or allies).
* **Sunbeam:** Best when affecting four or more creatures (enemies or allies).
* **Divine Judgment:** Cast when two or more allies are damaged to optimize healing.
* **Dazzling Light:** Best when affecting four or more creatures (enemies or allies).

#### Lore of Metal
Mage-priests of the Lore of Metal target creatures in heavy armor or wielding powerful weapons, leveraging the Metal Shifting trait.
* **Final Transmutation:** Targets low-hit-point creatures or those in heavy armor.
* **Plague of Rust (6th level):** Prioritizes targeting as many weapons as possible, then armor.
* **Weapon of Power:** Targets a creature in heavy armor, choosing Bludgeoning to push targets away, into Final Transmutation’s area, or toward Blades of Retribution.
* **Rebounding Blades:** Targets creatures in heavy armor with low Dexterity.
* **Slow:** Cast when concentration on *Plague of Rust* is lost.

#### Lore of Shadows
Mage-priests of the Lore of Shadows use debilitating and enhancing spells, leveraging Shadow Paths for optimal positioning.
* **Maddening Darkness:** Targets multiple creatures with low Wisdom saving throws.
* **Path of Shadows:** Moves allies across areas like *Maddening Darkness* or *Weird* after enemies reach them; drop *Maddening Darkness* if it hinders teleportation and all enemies have passed through its area.
* **Weird:** Cast after losing concentration on *Maddening Darkness*, targeting the same creatures to scatter foes and deny areas.
* **Synaptic Static:** Targets as many creatures with low Intelligence as possible.
* **Withering Resolve:** Targets a creature inside *Maddening Darkness* or *Weird*.

\pagebreakNum


##### Sload Mage-Priest Adventure Hooks
| d6  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Stirring Silence:** A sload mage-priest long thought dormant begins to stir, sending tremors through the jungle and shifting the stars above. Believing it has uncovered a piece of the gods’ forgotten design, it prepares to act, forcing the adventurers to choose whether to stop or aid a plan that could reshape the world.|
|  2  |**The Mind That Would Not Sleep:** A sload mage-priest has remained conscious for generations, and its overactive mind now warps reality itself. Magic storms rage, time fractures, and the priest’s attendants seek outside help to prevent their master from unraveling the very laws of nature. |
|  3  |**The Caged Prophet:** A cabal of mages has captured a living sload mage-priest and siphons its power through forbidden rituals. As rival factions gather to control (or destroy) it, the adventurers must navigate the chaos and decide its fate. |
|  4  | **Merciless Design:** A sload mage-priest has divined a corruption festering beneath a frontier settlement. Without warning, it commands its lizardfolk armies to raze the town, declaring that “The design must be upheld.” If the party defends the settlement, they risk facing the mage-priest’s overwhelming power head-on.|
|  5  | **Vile Facsimiles:** The players discover an ancient cloning facility being used by a mage-priest to bolster his army. However, the clones all possess a defective malevolence, including the sload mage-priest who is himself a clone that killed his original and stole his identity. |
|  6  |**Phases of Time.** A sload mage-priest orders the construction of five stone beacons, each aligned with an obscure lunar cycle. As the last beacon nears completion, time begins to warp; days pass in minutes, while other regions fall into stasis. The adventurers must navigate the temporal distortions to uncover the priest's plans.|

\columnbreak

### Sload Mage-Priest Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from sload mage-priests are the ancient relics they carry with them. However, some more macabre looters may harvest their remains for materials that hold some lingering power. Most carried valuables can be found using **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** checks. At the DM's discretion, harvesting their bodies can be done using an **Intelligence (Medicine)** check. 

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Sload Mage-Priest Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 1d6(3) 500gp Items |
|  10-12 | 2d4(5) 500gp Items | 
|  13-19 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  20-24 | 1d4(2) 2,000gp Items |  
|  25+ | 2d4(5) 2,000gp Items |

## The Wanderer

In the expansive lore of the lizardmen, a figure of myth and legend emerges from the mists of time, known only as "The Wanderer." This ancient crox is a living testament to battles past and a beacon of hope for the lizardmen in their darkest hours. He roams the lands, appearing where he is needed most and leaving countless legends in his wake.

Among the Crox, The Wanderer stands unparalleled — taller, broader, and evidently older than any of his kin. His body is a canvas of ancient scars, each narrating a saga of valor and struggle. Rather than typical armors, he's adorned with ceremonial artifacts, tokens from grateful tribes and tributes to the gods. Some of these tokens are so deeply embedded that they seem hammered into his very scales, becoming a part of him.

In battle, The Wanderer is a force of nature. He wields a massive maul, its weight and power enough to cleave through multiple adversaries in a single swing. His primal roar, a testament to his age and vigor, has the power to send enemies scrambling in fear and uplift the spirits of allies. But it's not just his weapon that foes should fear; with jaws capable of crushing bone, claws sharp enough to rend armor, and a tail adept at tripping those who venture too close, he's the embodiment of natural ferocity.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>



With every victory, The Wanderer doesn't just triumph over his adversaries, but he also wins the favor of the lizardmen deities. Each god values different facets of combat and nature, and through his myriad victories, The Wanderer touches upon each of their domains. Be it a fierce battle that pleases the god of storms, the hunt of a mighty monster that wins the respect of the god of beasts, or a saved lizardmen city that earns the smile of the goddess of protection, his actions resonate in the divine realms, cementing his status as their chosen champion.

Mysterious in his ways, The Wanderer has a knack for appearing when the lizardmen need him the most. At the brink of desolation, when all hope seems lost, his sudden emergence has turned the tide of many pivotal battles. With a natural instinct for leadership and strategy, he doesn't just fight; he leads the lizardmen, ensuring their survival and victory against overwhelming odds.

To the lizardmen, The Wanderer isn't just a warrior; he's a living legend, a spirit of the jungle, and an avatar of the gods. Every time he appears, they shower him with sacred relics, adding to his already vast collection of ceremonial adornments. These aren't mere gifts; they are tokens of reverence and sacrifice, symbolizing their deep devotion and dependence on the divine forces The Wanderer embodies.

____

> ## The Wanderer
> *Large monstrosity, lawful neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 18 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 299 (26d10 + 156)
> - **Speed** 40 ft., swim 40 ft.
> ___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|26 (+8)|10 (+0)|22 (+6)|6 (-2)|18 (+4)|10 (+0)|
> ___
> - **Saving Throws** Dex +4, Int +1, Wis +9, Cha +5
> - **Skills** Athletics +11, Perception +9, Stealth +5, Survival +9
> - **Condition Immunities** Exhaustion
> - **Senses** Darkvision 30 ft., passive Perception 19
> - **Languages** Draconic 
> - **Challenge** 16 (15,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&ensp;  **Proficiency Bonus** +5
> ___
>
> ***Cold Blooded.*** The wanderer has advantage on saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> ***Hulking Protector.*** Any ally smaller than the wanderer and within 5 feet of it has half cover, and its movement doesn't provoke attacks of opportunity. Allies can move through the space the wanderer occupies without it being treated as difficult terrain.
>
> ***Primal Roar (Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** When the wanderer's hit points drop to 150 or lower, any conditions that are incapacitating it end and it lets loose a roar. Every creature of the wanderer's choice within 120 feet of it that can hear the roar must succeed a DC 17 Wisdom saving throw or be frightened for one minute. Creatures frightened this way that end their turn 10 feet or more away from the wanderer can repeat the saving throw, ending the effect on a success. Additionally, the wanderer and allies of its choice within 120 feet of it enter a rampage for one minute. While rampaging this way, their weapon attacks deal an additional 5 (1d10) damage.
> 
> ### Actions
>
> ***Mighty Swing.*** The wanderer makes a Maul attack against any number of creatures within a 5-foot cube within 10 feet of it.
>
> ***Vice-like Jaws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 24 (3d10 + 8) piercing damage, and the target is grappled (escape DC 21). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the wanderer can't bite another target. If the bite hits a creature already grappled by the wanderer, the attack is a critical hit.
>
> ***Maul.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 22 (4d6 + 8) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ***Raking Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 15 (2d6 + 8) slashing damage. If the attack hits, the wanderer can immediately make another claw attack against the target as part of this action, but only once per turn.
>
> ***Tail Trip.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +13 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target not grappled by the wanderer. *Hit:* 17 (2d8 + 8) bludgeoning damage. If the target is a creature, it must make a DC 21 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone. If it fails the save by 5 or more, it cannot stand up until the end of its next turn.
>
> ### Legendary Actions
> The wanderer can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The wanderer regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
> 
> **Attack.** The wanderer makes one of its attacks other then Mighty Swing. Once it uses this action, it can't use the same attack as a legendary action until the start of its next turn.
>
> **Check.** The wanderer makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
> 
> **Move.** The wanderer moves up to 20 feet without provoking attacks of opportunity. If the wanderer is rampaging, it
moves toward the closest hostile creature it is aware of.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the wanderer is affected by a condition that allows a saving throw to end it either as an action or at the start/end of its turn, it can make that saving throw immediately with advantage. It can use this legendary action even if incapacitated. <br><br>
>

### Epic Battle:<Br> Favor of the Old Ones
For a mythic encounter with The Wanderer, increase his hit points to 600 HP and enhance his Primal Roar trait with the following effects. His Challenge Rating (CR) increases to 23.
Primal Roar Modification: The Wanderer's Primal Roar trait changes such that it triggers three different times as his hit points drop to 450, 300, and 150 rather than only triggering once. The damage bonus granted to allies from each roar can stack, and a single instance of damage to The Wanderer can trigger multiple roars.

Each time Primal Roar is triggered, a unique set of effects occurs. These effects persist until The Wanderer is reduced to 0 hit points or 10 minutes has passed.

#### 1st Roar (450 HP): The God of Beasts
The Wanderer's roar summons a **razorsaur** in an unoccupied space it can see within 300 feet, subject to the following conditions:
* The summoned razorsaur has an initiative count of 20 and benefits from the effects of the roar that called it forth, including having the rampaging condition.
* This razorsaur remains for 10 minutes or until either it or The Wanderer are reduced to 0 hit points.
* Each subsequent use of The Wanderer's Primal Roar will summon another razorsaur in the same manner.

\columnbreak

#### 2nd Roar (300 HP): The God of Storms
The Wanderer's roar summons a tempest blows around The Wanderer (30 miles per hour) and moves with it, remaining centered on it. The tempest is up to 1 mile high with a diameter of 150 feet. The Wanderer can choose any number of creatures to be unaffected by the storm, but all other creatures suffer the following effects while in its area:
* The storm is difficult terrain for flying creatures.
* Ranged attacks that travel more than 30 feet through the storm automatically miss.
* On initiative count 20, every creature within the storm must succeed on a DC 17 Strength saving throw or be pulled 30 feet toward its center.

#### 3rd Roar: The God of Protection
The Wanderer's roar creates a glowing 30-foot cube of shimmering magical protection centered on himself. He can choose any creatures within the area of the cube to be rendered immune to all forms of damage while they continue to be within it. The cube stays in one location and doesn't move with The Wanderer.

##### The Wanderer Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Wrath of The Wanderer:** In their travels, the players inadvertently anger a sect of lizardmen who view them as enemies of their god. The sect summons The Wanderer to quell the "threat" that the party supposedly poses.|
|  2  |**Jungle Plunder:** The players are visiting a jungle port town where many treasure hunters come to plunder the ruins within the mainland. The plundering soon awakens the ire of the lizardmen and their protector, The Wanderer. The players may join the treasure hunters to fight off the lizardmen and collect riches or aid the lizardmen in driving off the plunderers.|
|  3  |**The Imposter's Trick:** An imposter mimicking one of the players has grievously wronged The Wanderer or those he is charged with protecting. Mistaking the party for allies of the imposter, The Wanderer seeks them out for retribution. |
|  4  | **Primeval Clash:** The players come across The Wanderer in the deep jungle, where he is battling overwhelming numbers of giant beasts to earn favor with the gods. The players can aid him and attempt to earn his favor or stalk his exploits and try to scavenge for leftover loot in the aftermath.|

### The Wanderer Tactics 
The Wanderer excels in brutal melee combat. While formidable on his own, he becomes even more effective when supported by ranged creatures. These allies help compensate for his lack of long-range capabilities, and they work especially well together when the allies can benefit from The Wanderer's Hulking Protector feature.

\columnbreak

The Wanderer possesses an innate knack for battle tactics, akin to an animal's hunting instincts, and he can expertly maneuver both himself and his minions to target the most vulnerable foes.

When selecting from his attack options, you can make the following considerations:

**Mighty Swing.** This allows The Wanderer to use his maul to decimate the densest clusters of enemies on the battlefield.

**Vice-like Jaws.** This is effective against skirmishers like rogues and monks or ranged attackers. It prevents them from escaping, and The Wanderer can even move a grappled target into a cluster of enemies, setting them up for his devastating Mighty Swing.

**Raking Claw.** This attack is most effective against targets with low AC, ensuring that both claws hit their mark.

**Tail Trip.** Targets with low Strength are especially susceptible to this move and make for ideal targets.

#### Primal Roar
Once The Wanderer's Primal Roar ability triggers, all tactical considerations are cast aside in favor of pure bloodshed. However, he retains the capacity to utilize his legendary actions in the most tactically advantageous ways possible.


#### Mythic Encounter
The Wanderer's mythic battle presents a formidable challenge for a player party, demanding significant counterplay strategies.

For The Wanderer, there are few decisions to make. The primary tactical consideration involves positioning the razorsaurs upon their arrival. It's important to note that the newly-summoned razorsaur, in their rampaging state, will hurl spikes at the closest target. Ideally, they should be positioned to target ranged or flying attackers, which The Wanderer struggles to counter.

### The Wanderer Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from The Wanderer are the remains of the equipment he was using or valuables he was carrying. Though crox don't often collect these items themselves, other lizardmen often adorn them with bones, jewelry, and ornaments of precious metal for ceremonial purposes, and The Wanderer is decorated with the most sacred of these items. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

Because a battle against The Wanderer will likely be a major turning point in the adventure, it will often be a good idea to include a treasure hoard of the appropriate level as loot in addition to what's listed here.

#### The Wanderer Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.


##### The Wanderer Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 1 500gp Item |
|  10-11 | 1 1,000gp Item | 
|  12-17 | 1d4(2) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  18-23 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Items |  
|  24+ |  1d6(3) 2,000gp Items |  


##### The Wanderer Mythic Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-8  | 2d4(5) 5,000gp Items |
|  9-10 | 1d6(3) 10,000gp Items | 
|  11-17 | 2d4(5) 10,000gp Items  |  
|  18-23 | 1d6(3) 20,000gp Items |  
|  24+ |  2d4(5) 20,000gp Items |
